Qingdao Detains Another Batch of Antiquities 85

Japanese National Akata Yohei Detained at Qingdao Station for Transporting Antiquities

Consisting of over Ninety Pieces of Ancient Bronze Buddhas, Porcelain, and Woodenware

Qingdao Dispatch: A Japanese national residing in this city, Akata Kotaro, on the 19th of this month, purchased through-tickets from Beiping to transport eight large leather trunks of antiques. After the trunks were unloaded at Qingdao Station, station staff, recognizing that these were antiques and related to Chinese culture, deemed it inappropriate to release them immediately. The staff temporarily detained the items and reported the matter to the Railway Bureau for review. Upon receiving the report, the Bureau, to prevent the export of antiquities, specially notified the Qingdao Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau and Education Bureau to dispatch personnel to Qingdao Station at 11:00 AM on the 22nd to conduct a joint inspection. Those present included Sui Jiwu, head of the documentation section of the Jiaoji Railway Bureau; Wen Shao, a staff member of the Education Bureau; Deng Ji, a staff member of the Social Affairs Bureau; and Akata, the transporter, along with two other Japanese individuals. The boxes were opened one by one for inspection. The inventory totaled over ninety items, including ancient bronze Buddhas, porcelain, carved lacquerware, and woodenware, with woodenware accounting for approximately two-thirds of the total. After the inspection, the Railway Bureau sealed the boxes and entrusted them to Qingdao Station for temporary safekeeping. The inspection details were separately reported to the Municipal Government and the Jiaoji Railway Bureau, requesting instructions on how to proceed. The itemized inventory is listed below:

Box 1: Contains one small lacquer cabinet (cabinet doors inlaid with landscapes and figures made of gemstones), one polychrome flower plate, one small bamboo tea table, one small lacquer carrying box, three round lacquer wooden bowls.

Box 2: Two inlaid porcelain lacquer hanging screens, one inlaid with a vase and the inscription "Rub the jade to make it smooth, sweep and wipe to make it shine" in ten jade-inlaid characters, the other inlaid with the four figures of Fortune, Prosperity, Longevity, and Happiness, one large gold lacquer cabinet.

Box 3: One pair of white porcelain jue cups, one ceramic piece, one porcelain ding tripod, one small gold lacquer box, one green porcelain Buddha statue, one small lacquer cabinet (inlaid with jade stone figures), one wooden base, two small rectangular lacquer trays.

Box 4: One small rectangular carved lacquer table, one bean-green pure bowl, one small porcelain jar, one large lacquer box, two blue-flower porcelain bowls, one lacquer bucket, one bronze jue cup, one round small lacquer tea tray, one gilded ancient Buddha statue, two Daoguang large blue porcelain plates, one redwood lacquer carrying box, nine lacquer smoking pipe stems, one ancient bronze Buddha statue.

Box 5: One porcelain pillow, two tiger-shaped porcelain pillows, one clay seal, one wooden brush holder, one Yuan porcelain jar, one white porcelain jar, one imitation Song-Ming porcelain jar, one ancient pottery vase, one kiln-fired porcelain vase.

Box 6: One wooden mirror stand, one round lacquer rattan box, one Song porcelain jar, one bronze mountain with a small Buddha statue, two Song porcelain incense burners, one red lacquer leather box, one Duan inkstone, one red clay teapot, one reclining bronze Buddha statue, one bronze dragon-seated Buddha statue.

Box 7: One inlaid porcelain lacquer hanging screen, one large gold lacquer red cabinet.

Box 8: One string of lapis lazuli prayer beads, one small carved bamboo square screen, three earthenware dishes, one porcelain jar, one bronze lion incense burner, one rock-shaped wood piece with base, one Yuan porcelain bowl, one wooden base, one earthenware bucket, one Yixing clay teapot, one ancient bronze Buddha statue, one Song porcelain jar, one large square lacquer tray, one redwood small Buddha shrine with one gold-inlaid jade Buddha statue inside (said to be extremely valuable), one Longquan porcelain plate, one black Song porcelain vase, one Longquan porcelain washer, one black Yuan porcelain bowl, four porcelain bowls of varying sizes, one Ming porcelain bowl. (June 22nd)

Sacrifice of the Harbin Fire Brigade 86

Fire Erupts at Jewish Synagogue in Daoli

Eleven Firefighters Injured or Killed

Harbin Dispatch: At 4:20 AM on the 18th, a fire carelessly broke out at the Jewish synagogue on Paotai Street in Daoli. The fire initially was not large, but tragically, eleven firefighters were injured or killed in the line of duty, making it the most devastating firefighting incident in Harbin's history. The facts are summarized as follows:

Before and After the Fire 87

The Jewish synagogue was built over a decade ago, and its beams and pillars were decaying, no longer able to bear heavy loads. However, due to years of renovation, its exterior still appeared to be a well-maintained structure. Recently, the synagogue contracted workers to paint its exterior, and the golden-yellow walls shone brightly and beautifully. The work was still unfinished when, unexpectedly, around 4:00 AM on the 18th, a fire suddenly broke out inside, sending smoke and flames into the sky. The First Fire Brigade of the Municipality spotted the fire and immediately dispatched a team. As the synagogue was a tall, three-story building with a hollow interior and no place to climb, the fire originated between the ceiling and the roof, making it difficult to extinguish. Therefore, the fire continued to burn despite extended efforts. At 4:30 AM, the Second Fire Brigade of the Municipality and the Police Fire Brigade received the news and arrived to help, working together to put out the fire. By around 6:00 AM, the fire had subsided.

The Tragedy Occurs 88

At this time, the synagogue roof was still emitting dense smoke and flames. Russian and Chinese members of the First and Second Fire Brigades climbed onto the roof using ladders. They used axes and hooks to break open the roof tiles, hoping to locate the source of the fire. Unfortunately, the interior of the roof was partially destroyed by the fire and unable to bear the weight. With a loud crash, the entire roof collapsed, causing over ten Chinese and Russian firefighters working on the roof to fall from a height of over forty feet into the synagogue's interior. Simultaneously, the roof exploded, and broken beams, shattered pillars, and debris fell down, crushing the firefighters below. The remaining embers continued to burn. Firefighters working outside witnessed the disaster and immediately risked their lives to enter and rescue their comrades. They searched through the pile of beams, debris, and ashes, finding the injured and deceased firefighters. Most were covered in blood and ash, their faces blackened beyond recognition.

Two Firefighters Die 89

Wang Huayong, a firefighter from the First Fire Brigade of the Municipality, and Wang Furui, a firefighter from the Second Fire Brigade of the Municipality, died at the scene. The seriously injured survivors, Zhao Fengming from the First Brigade, and Liu Zhaohua, Ye Changsheng, Liu Shanghui, Tian Baoshan from the Second Brigade, along with the Second Brigade's Russian Deputy Captain Ivan Petrov, and Russian firefighter Guan Qinke, were transported to the First Municipal Hospital along with the deceased. Two others with minor injuries, Guo Huade and Jin Boxiang, were also taken to the hospital for treatment. On the afternoon of the same day, the bodies of the two firefighters who died were cleaned at the hospital and moved to the mortuary. The fire brigade purchased two coffins and clothing, immediately prepared the bodies for burial, hired two bands of musicians, and sixteen pallbearers. The funeral procession departed at 4:00 PM and proceeded to Jile Temple for burial. All firefighting teams in the city wore full uniform with black armbands, and lined the streets to pay their respects. Zhang Yintang, Secretary-General of the Special Municipality Bureau, representing the Mayor, led over fifty bureau section chiefs in the funeral procession. The Jewish synagogue that was burned had fire insurance coverage of 50,000 yuan, so the loss was minimal. The cause of the fire is still under investigation, and the authorities have dispatched personnel to conduct a thorough investigation. (18th)

Exhibition of Achievements by the Beijing Relief Home 90

The Beijing Relief Home's achievement exhibition opened on the 20th of this month. People in the capital, considering the exhibition an unprecedented event, flocked to visit out of a sense of social responsibility. The crowds were like a tide, and everyone remarked that the craftsmanship on display was dazzling. The best part was that it was all made up of everyday items, but they were able to incorporate clever ideas to make it new and exciting. Among them, the embroidery was particularly exquisite, and the educational achievements were also remarkable. The order within the exhibition was maintained by the junior boy scouts of the Relief Home's primary school, who kept everything running smoothly. The Relief Home's implementation of vocational relief has only been in place for eight months, but it has already achieved such remarkable results, making it a true beacon of hope for vocational prospects.

Wuhu Express 91

Chen Diaoyuan came to Wuhu to inspect the garrison troops. It is scheduled to take place on the 24th. The troops being inspected are the 57th Division artillery battalion, cavalry company, heavy mortar company, 171st Brigade 341st Regiment, and machine gun company.

The Li Family Grand Garden on Damalu in Wuhu has been renovated into a park. The Public Security Bureau is rushing to build the road outside the park to facilitate tourists. Today's bureau meeting also decided to name the road Gongyuan Road (Park Road).

It has been raining heavily here for days, and mountain floods have suddenly descended. The river tides have risen sharply. The Dongmen area has become a flooded region. Over ten thousand mu of fertile land on the Xingchun outer beach in this county were flooded last night, and the surrounding fields are also in imminent danger. Rescue efforts are underway day and night.

Recently, in order to promote machine irrigation, Central University specially sent Wu Guodong to bring an irrigation machine boat to Wuhu to contact the county government and demonstrate in the fields of Fangcun, Qingshuihe, and other towns. (22nd)

In order to quickly complete the Hanghai Section of the dike project, the Construction Department intends to temporarily partition the project and establish a separate engineering office directly under the department. In April, lake bandits looted Shiwanzhen. Director Shi of the Construction Department ordered the bureau to conduct a thorough estimate of the required funds. 4,000 yuan will be allocated from disaster relief public bonds from Hangzhou County, and 5,000 yuan will be subsidized by the Western Zhejiang Water Conservancy Deliberation Council to fund the construction.

Salt merchants in Jinhua, Tangxi, Lanxi, Yiwu, and other counties in eastern Zhejiang have been transporting quota salt from various fields via Shaoxing inland river vessels. Now, in reference to the success of salt transportation by automobiles in Lin'an, it is proposed to switch to railway transport. Since the salt merchants have now elected Chen Zuxiang to be stationed in Linpu to specialize in car transport of salt, they should also organize a transfer office, follow the salt firm's procedures, provide registration fees, and submit a guarantee to the department for registration.

In October, Cui was sent to the Zhenjiang District Court for investigation. Disputes Over Shops at Xuanmiao Temple Unresolved 97

The dispute over the reconstruction of shops on the original site of the screen walls on both sides of the main gate of Xuanmiao Temple has been going on for years and has not been resolved. This has led to a lawsuit in the district court between bowl merchant Jiang Lianfang and abbot Yan Juecang. The court ruled the previous day that the bowl shop buildings should be demolished immediately. The bowl merchant refused to accept the ruling and appealed to the High Court. On the 24th, the county political meeting resolved that the construction and public security bureaus should forcibly demolish the buildings to comply with the order of the Executive Yuan to build the screen wall.

Kidnapper Zhu Jiajun Executed by Firing Squad 98

Kidnapper Zhu Jiajun kidnapped the mother and wife of Li Xiaoping in his hometown of Xiao County last autumn. Li prepared funds to redeem them. Only Li's mother had her ears cut off and was released. Li's wife, Mrs. Ma, was raped, taken to Suzhou, and hidden in the southern garden. The District Prosecutor's Office sent police to Shanghai to arrest Zhu, who was sentenced to death. The sentence was submitted to the provincial government for approval. Yesterday morning (24th) at 8:00 AM, he was bound and escorted to Wangshudun outside the Changmen gate to be executed by firing squad. When the bandit was being bound, he cursed loudly and was stubborn. During the execution, he stood without kneeling and was killed by two shots. His skull flew more than four feet into the air.

Fierce Battle Between Peace Yushan Soldiers and Bandits 99

According to a telegram from Deputy Commander Wang Zhiqi of the Taihu Bandit Suppression Headquarters on the 24th, a team led by him killed a notorious bandit surnamed Yu in Mashan, Changxing on the 23rd, rescued a kidnapped child surnamed Zhang, and seized a set of bandit weapons, including a short-barreled gun and a pistol. In addition, the first platoon of the fifth company under his command encountered more than 30 lake bandits while searching and suppressing bandits in the Heye Yushan area on the 22nd and engaged in a fierce battle for two or three hours. Wuxi

Petition Regarding the Li Ashou Tragedy 100

Li Ashou, a carpenter at the Yeqin Yarn Factory outside the Dongmen, was delivering lunch to the Yongyu Silk Factory when he had a quarrel with Wang Yucheng, a factory guard. He was beaten to death by the guard and Song Ada, a rickshaw puller. After the various labor unions organized a support association, the support association held an executive committee meeting the afternoon before last and resolved the following: (1) Request the county party headquarters to uphold justice; (2) Request the county court to handle the Li case quickly and detain and prosecute Wu Xilin, the principal offender who instigated the murder; (3) Request the county government to dismiss and punish Wang Weixin, the chief of the Public Security Third Branch Bureau, for neglecting his duties and treating human life carelessly; (4) Request the Party, government, and judicial organs to investigate the case of bribing public opinion and seriously warn all sectors; (5) Telegraph all labor unions in the country to request unanimous support; (6) Telegram the central government to pay attention to the safety and security of workers' lives and to restore the vertical organization of labor unions. Yesterday morning (24th), thousands of representatives from various labor unions requested a petition to punish the murderers. The support association prepared a petition and gathered in the park. Executive committee members Wang Ciqing, Hui Jizhi, Sun Xiangfeng, Xie Bin, Gao Yisheng, Fan Tianxing, Chen Xiangchun, Gui Wochen, and Shen Gennan led the male and female workers to the county party headquarters to submit the petition, submit the petition face-to-face, and request permission to petition and uphold justice. Committee members Hu Nianqian, Zhang Renjie, Li Ti, and others came out to meet them. The nine representatives submitted the petition face-to-face and reported the case. Committee members Hu and others granted permission and appointed Lu Zhenwen to accompany them on the petition. The representatives resigned and then went to the county court to submit the petition. Chief Prosecutor Zhou Erkai received them. After the representatives explained the purpose of the petition, Chief Zhou said that the case was of great importance and he had ordered the detention center to stop Wang and Song, the two murderers in custody, from meeting with relatives and friends. The court will open this Saturday and summons have been issued. If Wu Xilin does not arrive by the deadline, he will be summoned for detention or put on the wanted list. In short, he will be dealt with in accordance with legal procedures and will never be let go. The representatives thought it was satisfactory and resigned. After reporting to the workers, they continued to go to the county government to petition. County Magistrate Pan Zhongjia met them in Wenxitang. After the representatives submitted the petition face-to-face, they requested that Wang Weixin, the chief of the Public Security Third Branch Bureau, be dismissed and investigated. County Magistrate Pan accepted the petition and promised to send a letter to the county court prosecutor's office to inquire whether Wang Weixin should be dismissed and brought to justice for questioning. He will then review and handle the case in a fair and impartial manner. Please pass this on to the workers and wait for news. The dismissal of the branch chief must be reported to the Civil Affairs Department for approval. This is in accordance with the prescribed procedures. The representatives resigned and told the workers before dispersing.

Strike at Shengyu Silk Factory 101

Fan Qingyuan, the chief driver of the Shengyu Silk Factory in Nanqiao Town, Yangming Township, Section 3 of Xiyi, has been managing twelve cars in the factory this year. He has repeatedly oppressed the female workers on weekdays, and the female workers have had to let him do whatever he wants in order to make a living. Recently, Fan has extended the working hours by more than 40 minutes per day, so some female workers were unwilling. They had staged a strike a month ago. Later, the labor union sent staff to the countryside to mediate and the matter was settled. However, the female workers of the factory went on strike for the second time the day before yesterday, saying that they would not work if Fan was in office and that they would resume work on the same day if Fan left office. Their attitude was very firm, and they made slogans and shouted together, "Down with Fan Qingyuan!" The reason for the strike was still due to the extended working hours. Manager Gao Shufang of the factory came out to settle the matter, and the staff of the silk factory labor union tried their best to persuade the female workers. As a result, the chief driver Fan Qingyuan voluntarily resigned. The working hours are still the same as before, and the female workers are satisfied and agreed to go to work as usual yesterday morning (24th).

Zhenjiang

Five Public Servants Gang Rape a Young Girl 110

Madame Chen Jiang, a widow from Jiangdu living at No. 5 Jiangjun Lane in the city, has no inheritance, only a daughter named Ruiying, sixteen years of age. The mother and daughter depend on each other to make a living, which is insufficient, so their relative, Jiang, provides assistance. Previously, due to the provincial capital moving to the town, Jiang opened Hengda Cigarette and Paper Store opposite the gate of the Civil Affairs Office to be close to his relatives. Because the store was small, Madame Chen Jiang prepared their meals daily, and her daughter delivered them. Over time, Xie Shaoqing, who worked as a clerk in the Education Office, saw Ruiying's beauty and became infatuated with her. He would flirt with her on the way, but the girl was unwilling to accept his advances and dared not refuse him, so she tried to avoid him. On the 7th of this month, Xie Shaoqing, unable to fulfill his desire for a long time, discussed the matter with his ten sworn brothers to devise a plan. That evening at ten o'clock, taking advantage of the quiet and dark, they invited Li Zhicai, Zhu Jianqing, Zhao Chunsheng, Zhang Chengzhi, and others to wait for the girl at the entrance of Baota Lane. When they saw her arrive, they stuffed a cloth into her mouth and dragged her to Wang Gengyun's house in Masi Lane, threatening her in every way, intending to marry her immediately. The girl refused, preferring death, but Xie Shaoqing and others forcibly gang-raped her. The girl was young and weak and could not withstand the violence, and fainted several times. Her mother waited until late at night and, seeing that her daughter had not returned, went to the store to inquire and learned that she had disappeared, and was heartbroken. Her relative, surnamed Jiang, had the girl's picture taken overnight and made multiple copies, which he presented to various military and police agencies, requesting investigation and arrest. Later, Deputy Officer Dong of the Security Department learned of the matter and negotiated with Xie and others to release the girl. After she told her story, everyone who heard it was outraged. Her mother hired someone to report the situation to the court prosecutor's office, which immediately issued arrest warrants. Court police officer Lu Fusheng arrested Xie Shaoqing, Xie Zhicai, Zhao Chunsheng, and Zhu Jianqing and brought them to court for questioning. Madame Chen Jiang testified as described above, while Xie equivocated. They were immediately detained. The details are still under investigation, and therefore cannot be fully disclosed at this time, but the prosecutor is conducting a thorough investigation and will severely punish them.

Pinghu

Mutiny of the Security Regiment Stationed in Xincang 119

The 16th company, 4th battalion, 7th regiment of the provincial security team stationed in Xincang Town in the eastern district of Pinghu and divided a platoon each to Yaqian and Xinmiao towns nearby, staged a mutiny. Company commander Guo Bin usually managed his troops strictly. Unexpectedly, at 2:00 AM on the 23rd, the soldiers from the two platoons stationed in Xinmiao and Yaqian secretly gathered in Xincang, tied up Company Commander Guo, and then went to the district office to demand 100,000 yuan in pay. District Chief Zhu Chenguang claimed that he was raising the money with local figures, so they forced him to go to the residence of Zhou Guiting, a local gentleman, and Ma Qibin, a standing committee member of the district party headquarters, to discuss a solution. Zhou Guiting took the opportunity to escape. Ma and Zhu were then injured by the mutinous soldiers. They then went to the Public Security Bureau to rob six guns and released seven bandits, including Jiang Lairong, instructing them to loot the entire town. The greatest losses were suffered by Xia Wanchang's jewelry store and Chongyu Money Exchange, totaling approximately 17,000 yuan. After looting, they went to Sancha River to loot the weapons of the local defense corps. They discovered that the local force was prepared, and their attack was thwarted, with the result that the local defense corps seized eleven rifles. At around ten o'clock, the mutinous soldiers looted two foreign goods stores in Huxiaoqiao Town and cut the telephone lines in the east market. In the afternoon, they went to Zhapu Town, first going to the chamber of commerce to demand money without success. They then guarded the four city gates, first looting the weapons of the Public Security Bureau, and then looting house by house. The Guangji pawnshop on West Gate Street suffered the greatest losses. All the rich merchants on the north and south river beaches were spared no loss. After looting, they swarmed to the seawall outside the south gate to seal ships and wait for the tide, preparing to escape by sea. On the morning of the 23rd, the various agencies in the county seat received the news and telegraphed the 7th Regiment Headquarters in Jiaxing and the Provincial Government and Security Department in Hangzhou. By 5:00 PM, two companies of security troops and several naval police ships had arrived from Jiaxing to pursue and arrest the mutineers. The naval police had already captured the mutineers Li Ronglin and a special commissioner on the afternoon of the 23rd and found several stolen goods on them, which have been sent to the local clearance bureau for disposal.

Cao Boquan, the magistrate of Zhenhai County, was suspended and detained for investigation due to dereliction of duty and bribery, after being accused by citizens. In addition, Zheng Yu was appointed by the provincial government to act as the magistrate of Zhenhai County and formally took over his duties yesterday.

Education News

Special Feature

The Great Revolution in the Japanese Education System and the Lessons for Our Country by Ma Zongrong 121

Education is like sunlight and air, something that everyone can take and no one can monopolize. However, in reality, the benefits of education, or rather, the freedom to receive education, are often occupied by a few. In other words, the current education system is too formalized and ignores social and economic conditions. As a result, those who obtain the equivalent of a junior high school education through self-study are often unable to enter high school because they lack a formal diploma, and those who obtain the equivalent of a high school education are often unable to enter university because they lack a high school diploma. On the other hand, the children of wealthy families can enroll in university, drift through for several years, and obtain bachelor's or master's degrees. We in the education field, after careful examination, are truly dissatisfied with the current formalized education system.

This feeling is not unique to us. Imperialist Japanese education scholars also have the same feeling. Therefore, taking advantage of this reform of the school system by the Japanese Ministry of Education, they have made many statements and suggestions to the Japanese Ministry of Education.

According to a Tokyo Dentsu News Agency dispatch on the 22nd of this month, the Japanese Ministry of Education held a meeting on the afternoon of the 31st to discuss and consider various opinions, and radically reformed the country's school system. The main points of the reform are:

1. Schools are only divided into three levels: elementary school, middle school, and university.

2. Free admission is permitted.

3. Night schools for young people are established for those who cannot attend school.

4. The entrance qualifications for each school are abolished to implement complete education.

The above education plan will be finalized this autumn and submitted to the Cultural and Political Review Committee for approval and implementation.

We know that "education" first arose among the wealthy class and intellectuals, most of whom had no worries about life. Therefore, the education systems formulated by them in various countries around the world are very formalized, naturally making it difficult for the children of the poor to receive education. However, the present era has become a society based on the masses. In order to achieve the strength of the entire people, all people should have the opportunity to receive education, and the formalized sports system should be reformed first. Imperialist Japan, a country where the classes of nobles and commoners still exist, a country that worships Western things in everything, still knows how to radically carry out a revolution in the school system: (1) Abolish the entrance qualifications for each school, and permit those with real ability to freely enroll; (2) Establish night schools for young people for those who cannot attend school. So what lessons can the Republic of China, a republic with equality for all people, a Republic of China that is revolutionary in everything, learn? I believe that our country's education authorities should pay attention to:

1. It is not appropriate to completely imitate the Western education system.

2. Abolish the entrance qualifications for each school, base everything on ability, and permit free application to the corresponding school.

3. Add night classes to all levels of schools.

Important News

Ministry of Education Handles Qinghua 122

The Qinghua University turmoil has dragged on for many days. According to a senior official of the Ministry of Education, external observations of the Qinghua incident are often inaccurate, leading newspapers to often use words such as mediation. In reality, this matter only involves handling and not mediation. Because President Wu is appointed by the government and has been explicitly retained to continue to be responsible. Even with the professors, they are only providing opinions, and the power to make decisions rests with the government. The Ministry of Education's handling of this matter has already been clearly pointed out in two points when President Jiang Menglin was telegraphed with the intentions: the regulations that have been revised cannot be changed, and the president should continue to serve. President Wu is still in Beiping handling school affairs as usual. The Ministry of Education still hopes that the professors can dispel misunderstandings so that school affairs can proceed and quickly return to normal. As for Mr. Qian Changzhao going to Beiping, Chairman Jiang instructed the Ministry of Education to send him to investigate, because the situation reported in the northern newspapers was too complicated, so Mr. Qian was sent to take a look in order to facilitate handling, etc.

Zhejiang Education Department Reappoints a Large Number of Principals 123

Eight Middle Schools and One Normal School

Previously, the faculty and staff of various provincial middle schools in Zhejiang Province, dissatisfied with the Director of Education Zhang Daofan, planned to collectively demand salaries and strike. Zhang, upon hearing the news, submitted his resignation and went to Beijing alone to avoid their criticism. The faculty and staff of various provincial middle schools, in the name of the Zhejiang Provincial Middle School Faculty and Staff Federation, telegraphed the Ministry of Education, requesting the prompt appointment of a worthy successor. After Zhang was retained by the provincial government and the central government and returned to Zhejiang to take office, the Ministry of Education considered the federation's interference in educational administration to be highly inappropriate and consulted with the Zhejiang Provincial Government to stop the federation's activities and order its dissolution. It is now known that the Department of Education has made considerable changes to the principals of various provincial middle schools. Details of the Week's Competition 143

Japanese Players Split Wins and Losses 丨 Sato Hyotaro Eliminated

British and American Forces Advance Smoothly 丨 Whiteley Shows His Skills

Women's Group Begins Competition 丨 Nat Holt Displays Power

London, 23rd Dispatch 144

Yesterday was the second week of the Wimbledon tennis tournament. After the rain, there were even more spectators than the first day. Women gathered, dressed in bright colors, around the center court. When Austin (Austin is the hope for British singles) entered the court in his school uniform, the crowd cheered for his victory.

Strong Player Sato Loses 145

Japanese Sato Hyotaro received a blow to the head yesterday in the second week, far from matching Austin. Austin's serve was as heavy as a shot, passing over the net like a hurricane. Sato could not resist his shots, Sato could only desperately defend the baseline, only passing it once or twice when Austin defended the net. Austin touched the net several times. In the end, Sato Hyotaro had no choice but to resign himself to fate. The scores were six to one, six to three, and six to zero.

Two of the Five Japanese Players Eliminated 146

Two of the five Japanese players were eliminated yesterday, Sato Hyotaro and Aoki. Aoki lost to Whiteley. The first set was fought to five to five. Aoki's weakness was fully exploited by Whiteley, so he lost. The difference in size between Sato Jiro and Rochus was almost astonishing. Rochus was exhausted from running around, while Sato moved around like a mouse from east to west. Sato constantly heavily drew back and quickly ran to the net, smashing with all his strength. Kawachi, only seventeen years old, was greatly praised for defeating Snowie yesterday.

British and American Forces Advance Smoothly 147

British and American players are progressing smoothly. Hillber, Hugh, Kingsley of England, and Wood, Shields, Lott, and Van Ryn of the United States all won.

Indian Players Emerge Exceptionally 148

Indian young player Mohan defeated Argentina's first-class player, Bauret, six to one, six to two, and six to one, causing a major upset and causing great surprise.

Only Argentina's Fruit Remains 149

After Argentina's Snowie lost to Japan's Kawachi, the only remaining fruit is Castillo.

Women's Barefooting is Interesting 150

De Courcel's defeat was disappointing, but the start of the women's group increased interest. Yesterday, former Spanish King Alfonso also came to the court to watch the women's competition. Coincidentally, Spanish female player Miss Tafolla and German Miss Sandt both entered the court barefoot without wearing socks. Many other female players imitated them and competed without wearing socks. Although the women's clothing conference has no explicit regulations, such dress has existed for several years, and the conference has informally expressed its disapproval.

Local News

Western Constable from Cross-Border Precinct Injures Chinese Police Officer on Haig Road 152

Arising from Minor Account Disputes

Will Become a Serious International Negotiation

Yesterday afternoon, Kong Qingfeng, a police officer from the Second Precinct of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau in Xujiahui, was shot and injured by Western Constable Harcott from the Jing'an Temple Police Station at the home of an American named Smith at 858 Haig Road. Haig Road is a road built by the Municipal Council beyond its boundaries. Police jurisdiction is in our country's hands, and it is under the jurisdiction of the Second Precinct of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau. This matter arose from a debt of thirty-five dollars, which was originally very trivial, but Smith was ignorant of the facts, leading to this unexpected incident. Details are as follows:

Debt Outstanding for Eight Months 153

An American named Smith, who works for an advertising company, lives at 858 Haig Road, which is numbered 25 in the Chinese area. In November of last year, he ordered three pairs of children's trousers and one coat from the Meidi Tailor Shop at 1934 near Jiaotong University on the same road, totaling thirty-five dollars. After the goods were delivered, Smith did not pay the debt. The shop owner, Yang Zhiqing, repeatedly demanded payment for eight months without receiving a penny. On the 14th of this month, Yang went to collect the debt again, as the Dragon Boat Festival was approaching. Smith reluctantly gave him a check from the Meifeng Bank, dated the 17th of this month, for thirty dollars.

Check Bounces 154

After receiving the check, Yang Zhiqing of the Meidi Tailor Shop used it the next day at the Tongxingxiang Cloth Shop in Xujiahui to pay a bill. Subsequently, it was transferred to other households. However, the last person holding the check was refused payment when they went to the bank to cash it. The check was then returned to Yang Zhiqing. Yang considered the bounced check to be worthless, so he went to Smith's place the day before yesterday to reason with him and demand the old debt. At that time, Smith's attitude was tough, refusing to exchange the check or pay the debt, making unreasonable arguments, pushing Yang out the door, and even beating and scolding him.

Report to the Public Security Bureau 155

At around 1:30 PM yesterday afternoon, Yang, along with Mao Fengxi, who opened a leather shoe shop nearby, went to return the check and demand payment. At that time, Smith was not home, but his wife received them, falsely telling Yang and others that she would go to the bank to withdraw the money and pay the debt, and then drove away in a car. Yang knew things were not good, so he reported the information to the nearby police post, who reported it to the Second Precinct of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau. Director Liu Yunfang then dispatched two police officers, Kong Qingfeng and Yan Lunxing, to investigate the situation and mediate.

Armed Western Constable Arrives 156

After leaving the house, the Western woman went to the Jing'an Temple Police Station to report an emergency, bringing an armed Western constable and a Chinese detective to the house. Two police officers from the Second Precinct of the Sixth District Public Security Bureau, Kong and Yan, were ordered to go there. However, as soon as they entered the door, disaster struck.

Western Constable Suddenly Opens Fire 157

The person sent by the Jing'an Temple Police Station was Western Constable Harcott, number 14. After Chinese policeman Kong Qingfeng entered the door, without asking any questions, Harcott pushed him out with force and immediately raised his gun and fired two shots. The second shot hit Kong in the right arm. Kong retreated with injuries and no longer advanced, immediately reporting to the station. Director Liu considered the situation to be serious and led several police officers to the scene to investigate.

Both Constables Disarmed 158

When the Director of the Second Precinct of the Sixth District arrived at the scene, the Sub-District Director of the Jing'an Temple Police Station, Sterbal, the Area Director of Area B of the Municipal Council Police Department, Weirather, the Area Detective Chief Clough, and the American Consul also arrived one after another. After negotiations by Director Liu, the offending Western constable was taken back under guarantee by the head constable, and both pistols were unloaded and taken to the station. Smith's debt was paid on the spot.

A Long Gun Found During Search 159

The Chinese police also found a long gun in Smith's home, with a bullet in the chamber that had not yet been ejected. It was said that Smith had raised the gun and made a shooting motion at the time. Since there was no municipal gun license, it was taken back to the station along with the Western constable's and the Chinese detective's pistols.

The Situation is Very Serious 160

At the time of the incident, the Jing'an Temple Police Station dispatched a large team of armed Chinese and Western detectives to the scene. At the same time, the Second Squad of the Police Corps stationed in Fahuazhen, upon learning of the situation, also sent dozens of car patrol teams and machine gun teams to the scene to maintain order. Traffic was cut off for a time, and the situation was serious. Director Liu considered the matter to be of great importance and reported it to the Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Chen, by telephone. Director Chen then personally went to the Second Precinct of the Sixth District in Xujiahui. Later, Western Detective Chief Clough and Head Constable Sterbal, along with Director Chen, repeatedly discussed the matter and guaranteed medical expenses, so the matter was resolved soon, and the storm temporarily ended.

Post-Incident Negotiations 161

It is heard that Director Chen, for the sake of prudence, intends to propose four solutions: (1) Compensation for medical expenses, (2) A formal apology to the authorities, (3) A guarantee that unfortunate incidents will not occur again in the future, and (4) In the future, all actions by the personnel of the concession police station, including Chinese and Western constables, on roads built beyond the boundaries must not be taken without the permission and formal notification of the Public Security Bureau of the relevant district.

Municipal Finance Bureau Schedules Collection of Business Tax 162

Regulations Have Been Reported to the Ministry for Record

The Municipal Business Tax has been in preparation by the Municipal Civil Affairs Bureau, which established a preparatory office. The draft of the business tax collection regulations, implementation rules, and tax rate tables were all drafted by the preparatory office, which invited representatives from the Chamber of Commerce to participate in discussions and agreed to begin collection on July 1. The preparatory office has now submitted the revised drafts to the Municipal Finance Bureau, which has forwarded them to the Municipal Government for submission to the Ministry of Finance for record. The original consultation and drafts are disclosed below:

Consultation 163

The Municipal Government consults the Ministry of Finance, stating: "Regarding the matter of consultation, according to the report of Cai Zengji, Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau and Director of the Business Tax Preparatory Office, 'Reporting the submission of the draft of the Municipal Business Tax Collection Regulations and Implementation Rules and Tax Rate Table for review and approval.' It is found that the business tax, according to Article 9, Section 3 of the Municipal Organization Law, is a type of municipal financial income. The Ministry previously ordered preparations to be made, considering Shanghai to be the most prosperous commercial area in the country, as well as a place where Chinese and foreigners live together, its situation is very different from other provinces and cities. If the planning is not thorough, the handling will be difficult. Therefore, since the establishment of this office, the drafting of all regulations has carefully considered the situation in Shanghai and made prudent considerations in order to facilitate future implementation and avoid conflicts. Now, with reference to the Ministry of Finance's 'Outline and Supplementary Measures for the Collection of Business Tax in Various Provinces,' we have separately drafted three drafts: 'Municipal Business Tax Collection Regulations and Implementation Rules' and 'Curriculum Standards Tax Rate Table,' and have repeatedly invited representatives from the Chamber of Commerce, Wang Yansong, Fang Jiaobo, Luo Qinghua, Zhu Wenqi, Chen Songyuan, etc., to participate in discussions, jointly discuss, and revise the original tax rates, regulations, and implementation rules according to different situations. The tax rates have been reduced as much as possible, and the collection methods have also been simplified as much as possible in order to facilitate implementation. The drafts have now been completed and submitted to the Ministry for review and registration for the sake of public convenience.' Accordingly, the draft is enclosed and submitted to the Ministry for review and registration, sincerely wishing for public cooperation. This consultation is to the Ministry of Finance."

Regulations 164

Draft Regulations for the Collection of Business Tax in Shanghai Municipality, Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with Article 8 of the Outline for the Collection of Business Tax promulgated by the Ministry of Finance and the supplementary regulations. Article 2: All operators of various businesses listed in Article 4 within the Shanghai Municipal area shall be subject to business tax in accordance with these regulations, unless otherwise stipulated by laws and regulations. Article 3: Business operators who meet the following conditions shall be exempt from business tax after verification: (1) Those with business capital of less than 500 yuan; (2) National or municipal businesses; (3) Businesses not for profit. Article 4: The standards and rates for business tax assessment shall be separately stipulated in a schedule. Article 5: For sales businesses that engage in wholesale, the business tax on the wholesale portion may be paid at a fixed rate of one-quarter. The wholesale business mentioned in the preceding paragraph refers specifically to wholesalers dealing with each other. If a business engages in both wholesale and retail, the tax amount shall be calculated separately. Article 6: The calculation of business capital shall be based on the paid-up capital. However, various reserve funds of limited companies shall be regarded as capital and taxed at one-third of the capital amount. Article 7: If various businesses have branches within the Shanghai Municipal area, their business tax may be paid by the head office in one lump sum. If the head office or branch is located outside the municipality, only the branches or head office located within the municipality shall pay business tax. If the capital cannot be divided and calculated, the competent tax collection agency shall estimate the taxable amount. If there is any objection, it shall be handled in accordance with Article 13. Article 8: If a store engages in several types of business with different tax rates, the tax amount shall be calculated based on the main business activity. Article 9: Manufacturers who directly retail their manufactured goods shall pay tax on the direct retail portion at the tax rate prescribed for manufacturing, without being subject to additional business tax for sales. Article 10: For businesses where the taxable standard is based on turnover, capital amount, or other calculated amounts, the total tax revenue shall be assessed based on the estimated annual business income or capital amount, and other calculated amounts. The total annual tax revenue shall be determined according to the tax rate and divided into four seasons for collection (the amount collected each season is one-quarter of the annual tax amount). For newly established businesses, the business tax shall be calculated from the quarter in which they begin operations. Article 11: When business tax is implemented, the competent tax collection agency may, in accordance with the following provisions, dispatch personnel to conduct a joint investigation with the chamber of commerce, compile a tax register, and prepare a business license. The license shall be stamped by the relevant trade association and forwarded by the chamber of commerce to the competent tax collection agency for issuance. If there is no trade association, the chamber of commerce shall apply on their behalf. Subsequently, in the first month of the following year, the business operator shall fill out a report form and request a renewal of the business license, following the same procedure. Newly established businesses shall submit a report form before commencing operations to obtain a license, stating: (1) The type and name of the business and its location; (2) The name, native place, and address of the business operator; (3) The amount of business capital; (4) The estimated annual business income. The business license shall be renewed annually without any fee. However, those who are exempt from tax in accordance with Article 3 shall pay a license fee of 2 jiao (0.2 yuan). Article 12: For businesses where the taxable standard is based on turnover or other calculated amounts, the business operator shall calculate the turnover or other calculated amounts at the end of each year and report it to the competent tax collection agency before January 15th of the following year. However, if the business terminates in less than one year, it shall be reported at the time of termination. Article 13: If a business operator fails to submit a report or submits a false report in accordance with Articles 11 and 12, the competent tax collection agency may dispatch personnel to investigate and verify the taxable amount. If the business operator objects to the decision of the competent tax collection agency, they shall submit a report to the Finance Bureau, which shall refer it to the review committee for assessment. This procedure shall also apply to objections to the decision of the competent tax collection agency when the business tax is implemented. The investigation mentioned in the preceding paragraph shall be conducted by the competent tax collection agency jointly with representatives from the chamber of commerce and the relevant trade association. Article 14: The organization and rules of procedure for the review committee shall be determined separately. Article 15: When collecting business tax, the competent tax collection agency may, when necessary, inspect the account books, documents, and goods of the business operator, but it must be done in conjunction with the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Without the approval of the review committee, the account books, documents, and goods shall not be removed from the inspected store for investigation and inspection. Article 16: If a business operator suspends operations, transfers ownership, relocates, reorganizes, or increases capital, they shall immediately report it to the competent tax collection agency, surrender the old license, and apply for a new license. Article 17: If a business license is lost or damaged, a new license shall be obtained upon payment of a license fee of 2 jiao (0.2 yuan). Article 18: If a business operator underreports business income, capital amount, or other calculated amounts, conceals information, operates without a license, or delays tax payment, once discovered or reported, the competent tax collection agency shall submit a report to the Finance Bureau, which shall refer it to the review committee for review and punishment. The penalties shall be determined separately. Article 19: The Finance Bureau shall issue a monthly notice regarding the collection of business tax and prepare an annual credit record, which shall be reviewed and signed by the review committee before being published. Article 20: All existing levies and taxes in the municipality that are similar in nature to business tax shall be renamed business tax and shall be temporarily collected at the original tax rates. Article 21: For businesses not listed in the schedule in Article 4 that are subject to business tax, the Finance Bureau may propose the applicable tax rates and submit them for approval. Article 22: The detailed implementing rules for these regulations shall be determined separately. Article 23: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Detailed Rules 165

Draft Detailed Implementing Rules for the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Regulations, Article 1: These detailed rules are formulated in accordance with Article 22 of the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Regulations. Article 2: The collection of business tax shall be handled by offices established by the Finance Bureau based on local conditions. However, in special circumstances, it may be entrusted to other agencies. Article 3: All business operators within the Shanghai Municipal area, regardless of whether they are subject to business tax regulations, shall comply with the provisions of Article 11 of the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Regulations and apply for a business license. Article 4: Business operators shall maintain account books and record the following items: (1) Detailed number of goods and raw materials purchased; (2) Detailed number of goods sold; (3) Daily cash inflows and outflows; (4) Monthly totals; (5) Annual totals. Article 5: The competent tax collection agency shall maintain a business tax register, listing the items prescribed in Article 11 of the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Regulations, classified and recorded. The format of the register shall be determined separately. Article 6: The competent tax collection agency shall review and determine the type of business and the amount of business tax payable based on the investigation report of the investigators or the report submitted by the business operator. Article 7: Once the amount of business tax payable by a business operator has been determined by the competent tax collection agency, it shall not be reduced or increased within one year, unless otherwise stipulated by laws and regulations. Article 8: For businesses subject to taxation, if the annual business income or capital amount, and other calculated amounts, are less than 1,000 yuan, the taxable amount shall be calculated by rounding to the nearest thousand. Article 9: When collecting business tax, the competent tax collection agency shall prepare a monthly collection receipt and issue it to the tax collector for collection. Article 10: The business license of a business operator shall be displayed in a conspicuous place in the store for inspection. Article 11: The report form to be filled out by business operators when applying for a business license shall be prepared by the Finance Bureau and distributed to the competent tax collection agency for use. The format shall be determined separately. Article 12: If a business operator disagrees with the taxable amount when paying business tax, the competent tax collection agency shall provide a detailed explanation of the investigation and, if there is evidence, submit the evidence to the Finance Bureau for handling in accordance with Article 13 of the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Regulations. Article 13: If the report on the taxable standard amount submitted by a business operator is certified by a chamber of commerce or accountant (a limited company shall be certified by an accountant), the investigation procedure may be waived. However, if the competent tax collection agency has any doubts, it shall still be handled in accordance with Article 13 of the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Regulations. Article 14: For businesses jointly owned by government and merchants, only the merchant's share shall be subject to business tax. Article 15: If there are any matters not covered in these detailed rules, the Finance Bureau may amend them at any time and submit them to the Municipal Government for approval and record. Article 16: These detailed rules shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

The Ministry of Military Affairs Dispatched Commissioners Yesterday to Inspect the Wusong Fortress 166

Registers Were Separately Completed and Returned to the Capital to Report on Their Mission

Liu Guangyan, a section chief specially dispatched by the Ministry of Military Affairs, and Li Dexuan, a clerk, arrived in Shanghai to inspect the Wusong Fortress. They were received by Commander Deng Zhenquan, who immediately ordered Chen Yuwen, commander of the South Shitou Battery; Wu Changqing, commander of the North Battery; Shi Ze, commander of the Lion Grove Battery; and Gu Ding, commander of the garrison battalion, to assemble their respective troops in preparation for inspection. Subsequently, Teng Jushou, the chief of staff of the headquarters, and Zhu Song, the officer on duty for the

Page 14

day, accompanied them to the North and South batteries, inspected them in sequence, and surveyed the various gun emplacements. They then proceeded to the garrison battalion to inspect the infantry, after which they returned to the headquarters for lunch. After lunch, they continued to the Lion Grove Battery for inspection and then went to the Sanguantang to survey the general gunpowder depot. Upon completion of the inspection, they separately filled out the registers and, at approximately 5:00 PM, returned to Shanghai by the same vehicle to return to the capital and report on their mission.

Domestic Cotton Production Statistics for the Past Five Years 167

Cotton Fields Totaling 37,593,012 Mu

Cotton Production Totals 8,800,956 Dan

丨Investigation by the Shanghai Chinese Cotton Mill Association丨

Since 1919, the Cotton Production Statistics Department of the Chinese Cotton Mill Association has dispatched personnel to the cotton-producing provinces and regions within the country to conduct on-site investigations of cotton production. These investigations have continued for twelve years without interruption. In recent years, due to considerable cooperation with the leading cotton farms and cotton industry organizations in various provinces and regions within the country, progress has gradually been seen. In 1930, the Association completed its investigation and final estimation of domestic cotton production (including Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan provinces). The findings were published, revealing a total of 37,593,012 mu of cotton fields and 8,800,956 dan of seed cotton produced. The final estimated figures for cotton fields and production amounts for the past five years are listed below for comparison:

Year　　　Cotton Fields (Unit: Mu)　　　　　Production Amount (Unit: Dan)

1930　　37,593,012　　　　　8,800,956

1929　　33,811,255　　　　　7,586,958

1928　　31,926,311　　　　　8,839,274

1927　　27,610,276　　　　　6,722,108

1926　　27,349,727　　　　　6,243,385

The figures for 1928 and 1929 have been revised and therefore differ from the previously published numbers. Detailed figures for each province can be found in the China Cotton Production Statistics published by the Association.

Tan Yunshan, Who Represented the National Government as a Special Envoy, Discusses the Situation in Tibet 168

Lamenting Xie’s Close Relationship with the Dalai Lama, but His Death Before Reaching Tibet

The War Originated from a Minor Incident; the People’s Hearts Return to the Central Government

Tan Yunshan, the chief writer for the Xing Shang Chinese Overseas Newspaper in Myanmar, who formerly accompanied Xie Guoliang, a special envoy dispatched by the National Government, on a mission to Tibet for investigation, has been preparing to leave Shanghai for Nanjing today after arriving in Shanghai on the 20th of this month. Mr. Tan will replace Mr. Xie in reporting everything to the National Government, as Special Envoy Xie Guoliang died en route. Before leaving Shanghai, Mr. Tan spoke in detail with a reporter from Xin Sheng She about the latest situation in Tibet and his experiences in Tibet. The details of his talk are recorded below in separate sections:

Journey to Tibet 169

Mr. Tan said that Special Envoy Xie's mission to Tibet was initially undertaken only with his son. When they reached Maymyo in Myanmar, Xie's son fell ill and died there. Feeling inconvenienced by being alone and being advanced in age, he greatly desired an assistant. Subsequently, Master Shoushi of Fayuan Temple in Beijing introduced him (Mr. Tan referring to himself) to go with him. In early November of last year, while crossing the Himalayas, Xie became ill. After traveling for more than 20 days, the Dalai Lama in Lhasa heard the news and sent people to greet them. One day before arriving in Lhasa, Mr. Xie died of his serious illness. After arriving in Lhasa, the Dalai Lama had a deep old friendship with Xie, so the funeral was held with great ceremony. After Xie's death, I was responsible for the investigation and conveying the intentions of the central government. I stayed in Lhasa for about three months. Due to the inconvenience of transportation and being secretly monitored by the guards sent by the Dalai Lama, I did not travel elsewhere. On February 15th, I left Lhasa and on March 13th, I returned to Calcutta in India. I traveled in India for two months. On May 18th, I returned to Yangon in Myanmar. On June 1st, I left Yangon, on the 13th, I arrived in Hong Kong, and on the 16th, I transferred to a ship to Shanghai, arriving on the 20th. I am now scheduled to take the Shanghai-Nanjing train to Nanjing on the morning of the 25th or tomorrow evening to report to the National Government, he said.

Political Overview 170

The Tibetan side has no politics to speak of. The Tibetans are superstitious about lamas, so politics and religion are not separate. Political power is entirely in the hands of the lamas, hence the name "monastic politics." The person currently in power is the Dalai Lama, who resides in Lhasa, the capital of Tibet. His power is vast and unrestricted by law. He can do whatever he wants. Beneath the Dalai Lama is the Tibetan King, but this is an official position in name only and is also the Dalai Lama's nephew. Below the King are four "Kalons" (meaning ministers). The four Kalons also do not have separate responsibilities, they merely execute all orders of the Dalai Lama. Before 1922, Tibet was ruled by the Dalai Lama, and Tibet was ruled by the Panchen Lama, who resided in Xigaze. Now that the Panchen has been expelled, both Tibet are ruled by the Dalai Lama.

Military Situation 171

In military affairs, Tibet had no formally trained army in the past. However, in recent years, influenced by the world's scientific advancement, a formal army organization has begun. However, their numbers are still not large, with an estimated total of just over 6,000 soldiers. The person in charge of these forces, according to the Tibetan term, is a Director-General. Below him are thirteen "Daizhang," meaning thirteen battalions. Each Daizhang has approximately 500 soldiers. In addition, there are civilian soldiers and lama soldiers who can be mobilized or recruited at any time, similar to a conscription system, with national reserves and auxiliary forces. The source of their military equipment is mostly from England, India, Japan, Russia, and other places. Although Lhasa, the capital, also has a machinery bureau, it is small in scale and can produce only twenty or thirty rifles each year. Within its internal organization, there is only one Han Chinese as an engineer who also teaches Tibetans how to manufacture firearms.

Transportation Facilities 172

In transportation, travel is very inconvenient due to the mountainous terrain of Tibet. Other than the railway set up by the British in Darjeeling that reaches Yatung in Tibet, there are no other railways, post offices, telegraph offices, etc. Except for the route from Lhasa to Gyantse, which belongs to Tibet, and from Gyantse to the Indian border, which belongs to Britain, the rest of the region has no postal or telecommunications facilities. Official documents and correspondence are still transmitted in the same way as the ancient post station system. There is now a long-distance telephone line from Lhasa to Gyantse and then to Yatung. Its jurisdiction is the same as the post and telegraph.

Commercial Situation 173

Aside from those Tibetans who devoutly believe in lamas, shave their heads to become monks, and engage in nomadic life, few engage in commerce. Therefore, the majority of its commercial power still belongs to people from Sichuan and Yunnan provinces, especially Muslims, who mainly deal in tea and silk. Although Indians occasionally engage in the tea business, Tibetans generally do not welcome them, as they are accustomed to drinking Chinese tea. The British have no economic power in Tibet. The goods imported from India are mostly cloth, furniture, kerosene, and alcohol, while the exports are wool, cowhide, musk, etc. The central government has no customs collection facilities in Tibet. However, in the Pagri region, the Dalai Lama has set up a taxation agency that only collects export taxes and not import taxes.

Strange Customs 174

Tibetans still hold deep superstitions. Many men prefer to become lamas. Those who do not shave their heads to become monks often have several brothers sharing one wife. This affects the ethnicity. Funerals are divided into four types: sky, earth, water, and fire. Sky burial is the most common, where the corpse is dissected with sharp knives and then transported to remote mountains or wilderness to be eaten by birds and beasts. Earth burial is rare, only used for those who die from epidemics or infectious diseases. Water burial is mainly for the poor who cannot afford other options. Fire burial is exclusively for lamas. Regarding clothing, officials often wear old Qing Dynasty official attire. In terms of diet, they mainly eat tsampa mixed with butter. Tsampa is roasted barley flour mixed with butter and tea, called butter tea. Mr. Tan said that this item has a good flavor. When I was in Tibet, I used it as a substitute for rice. I also liked to eat it. While speaking, he showed the reporter tsampa flour.

Other Recent News 175

When I was in Lhasa, the Xikang war had already broken out. The cause was the trivial matter reported in the newspapers. If one only looks at the Dalai Lama's attitude, it seems good on the surface. However, he secretly harbors the ambition to exclusively control all of Tibet and Xikang. However, observing the general public's sentiment, they all lean towards the central government and hope that the national government will have appropriate measures to connect them with the country. As for the rumors that there are British people instructing them, according to my personal observation, this may not be true. The British have no significant power in Tibet. The Dalai Lama is good at using them. The British troops in Tibet are only fifty in Yatung and fifty in Gyantse, and they are not purely British troops, mostly Nepalese troops. Their economic power is also very weak, only the goods imported from India as described above. Although the annual trade volume is not known for sure, judging from the general situation, the number is not very large.

The Revival of the Chinese Domestic Goods Market is Near

### Yang Zhao Yun's Protest Results 176

After the closure of the Chinese Domestic Goods Market, Yang Zhao Yun, the president of the Special District Local Court, repeatedly questioned the Public Works Department (工部局) and personally visited Fei Xindun (費信惇), the supervisor of the Public Works Department, to protest and requested that they must handle matters according to legal procedures in the future. Now, we have obtained two recent letters between the court and the Public Works Department, which are hereby disclosed. Since the Public Works Department has the sincerity to resolve this case and acknowledges that the previous measures were due to misunderstanding and expressed regret, the date of the Chinese Domestic Goods Market's reopening should not be far away. (Public Letter from the Shanghai Special District Local Court) Dear Sirs, regarding the case of your department instructing the police to forcibly close the Chinese Domestic Products United Market, this court sent a letter on June 12 inquiring about the details of the matter, but has not yet received a reply. Now, the United Market has submitted a petition stating that the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, due to the entertainment section's equipment issues, did not file a suit with this court for a hearing and judgment beforehand, but abruptly sent police to order the suspension of business and sealed off the entire market, prohibiting employees from entering and exiting, which is illegal and exceeds their authority, requesting relief. If the entertainment section of the market violates the regulations, it is a violation of regulations and should be litigated to this court for clarification and handling according to the law. Now that your department has closed the market without going through this procedure, it is difficult to consider it legal. Accordingly, we request your department to investigate and order the complete withdrawal of the police guarding the market, allowing the market to operate as usual. If there are legal issues, your department's representative lawyer can still file a lawsuit with this court according to the law, and this court will naturally handle it according to the law. In the future, if there are similar incidents, please still follow the legal procedures to avoid disputes and clarify jurisdictions. We also hope to receive a reply. Sincerely, Yang Zhao Yun, President of the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department. (Reply from the Public Works Department) Dear Sir, received your letter of June 22, regarding the Chinese Domestic Goods Market, requesting that this court follow legal procedures for cases of violation of regulations, as per usual practice. There are many misunderstandings in this case, which is truly unfortunate. Now, representatives of our department and the Domestic Goods Market have negotiated and agreed on appropriate measures to handle the aftermath with careful consideration. Sincerely, Fei Xindun, Supervisor of the Public Works Department, to Yang, President of the Shanghai Special District Local Court. June 23.

Committee Letter Requesting Assistance 177

The Chinese National Products Market Negotiation Committee sent letters to various assistance groups yesterday, stating: Respectfully, the Chinese National Products United Market was abruptly illegally closed by the Public Works Department of the Public Concession on June 9, and the various unfortunate incidents of assaulting and arresting employees are presumably well-known. We are deeply grateful for the righteous assistance of the members of your esteemed association. The most essential part of the negotiation process is that on June 19 and 20, Mr. Yu Qiaqing (虞洽卿) notified representatives from both sides to talk at the City Chamber of Commerce. Mr. Wang Xiaolai (王曉籟), in his capacity as temporary chairman, certified that the reports of the representatives from our association, Hong Yan (洪雁), Li Weicheng (李維城), and Chen Weixin (陳維新), were completely true, and recognized that the Public Works Department's closure of the market in batches was a major mistake, which shows that justice will eventually triumph over power. Now, our association has separately sent letters to our government regarding the Public Works Department's violation of the agreement and infringement of legal rights, raising protests, and has also decided on seven measures to seriously negotiate with the Public Works Department to protect the safety of Chinese taxpayers. We are immensely grateful.

Sending Committee Members to Make Contact in Different Ways 178

Communist Zhang Qian Arrested 180

Subversive Publications Found

Accomplices Not Captured

At 7:30 PM the night before last, detectives from the Putuo Road police station arrested a man named Zhang Yimin (張逸民) on Robison Road. Zhang is from Hubei. According to his own statement, his real name is Zhang Qian (張潛), 32 years old. Yimin is his alias to avoid attention. He holds some kind of position in the Third District Committee established by the Communist Party in Hubei, with a monthly salary of 30 yuan. He was sent to Shanghai for secret activities two months ago, residing at No. 111 Kangnuotuo Road in the Chinese area. The 200 subversive leaflets he carried were ordered by an accomplice named Luo to be brought to Robison Road and handed over to someone wearing a woolen scarf. However, he waited for a long time and did not see that person. He heard that Luo is currently residing in Wuding Lane, Wuding Road. The police chief immediately ordered detectives to search Zhang's residence. Under Zhang's bed, they found two subversive publications, "Road to Light" and "International Monthly," and a letter. They then went to Luo's residence, but Luo had already escaped beforehand. The search yielded nothing else. Yesterday morning, Zhang was escorted to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Judge Gao held a court session for interrogation. After the police lawyer presented the case, detectives Zhang Youming (張有明) and Zhao Fuhai (趙福海), and Western detective Hua Tuo, successively reported the process of capturing the defendant and submitted the leaflets, books, and letter to the court for review. Zhang Qian, when questioned, reversed the statements he made at the police station, saying that he came to Shanghai from Hubei this time to apply for admission to Jiangnan School, and that the leaflets he had found on the road, and the books in his residence belonged to a friend named Zhuang. Judge Gao then ordered the defendant to be remanded and adjourned the hearing for further investigation.

Railroad and Telephone Poles Broken by Hurricane Last Night 184

Telegraph and Telephone Lines Cut Off

Beijing-Shanghai Trains Proceed Slowly

Around 8:00 PM last night, a hurricane occurred in the Changzhou to Danyang area of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, and the telegraph poles along the road were blown down, cutting off telegraph and long-distance telephone lines. Therefore, the Beijing-Shanghai trains passing through the area had to proceed slowly to avoid danger.

Tang Huixuan Requests Mediation for Divorce from Zou Aizhen 185

Submits Petition to the Special District Court

Willing to Sacrifice All Property

Tang Huixuan (唐惠玄), a doctor of economics, previously reported to the police that his wife, Zou Aizhen (鄒愛貞), had an affair with Chen Genwei (陳根偉), and the police were dispatched to arrest Zou and Chen and send them to the Shanghai District Court Procuratorate for investigation. Zou immediately filed a lawsuit against Tang for bigamy and false accusation. The lawsuit between them has lasted for nearly a year, and the newspapers have broadcast it, and society has talked and laughed about it. Now, Zou Aizhen's request for divorce from Tang Huixuan is still in progress at the Shanghai District Court. Tang has moved to the Public Concession, so he did not appear in court within the city. He also hired lawyer Yuan Yang'an (袁仰安) to file another petition with the Special District Court, requesting mediation for divorce and asking Zou to hand over the two children born to them so that he could take them back to raise. The mediation petition stated that Tang Huixuan married Zou Aizhen in the United States in October of the Republic of China Year 12. At that time, Tang was a professor in the United States. In Year 15, Zou returned to China first with their two children because she was weak after childbirth and lacked care. Tang gave Zou approximately $4,000 USD, earned from years of hard work, to take back. After arriving in Shanghai, Zou lived with her mother and sister on Zhonghua Road and purchased land in Longhua. The remaining funds were deposited in the bank. The following year, Tang returned to Shanghai from the United States and lived with Zou, with affection as before. Later, Tang went out to work and was separated from her from time to time. Then, a person named Chen Genwei falsely recognized Zou's mother as his godmother and was able to live with Aizhen, and an affair occurred. In August of the year before last, Tang returned from a business trip and felt that Zou's attitude towards him had completely changed and that she was becoming increasingly intimate with Chen. He knew there was something wrong, but out of years of love, he couldn't bear to break off with her abruptly and tried to persuade her to repent gently. Later, he left Shanghai again to work, continuously sending more than 3,000 yuan for living expenses. Last summer, he returned from Guangdong, but Zou refused to live with him and behaved as if she was a couple with Chen, which was truly unbearable. He reported to the First Section of the First District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and the police were dispatched to Zou's house to arrest Zou and Chen and hand them over to the Shanghai District Court for repeated interrogations. Later, Tang followed advice and withdrew the charges, while Aizhen sued Tang for bigamy and false accusation. As a result, the judgment was rejected, and the lawsuit ended. Tang once visited Zou's house on Zhonghua Road, but did not meet with Aizhen. However, Aizhen at this time filed a petition with the court for divorce from Tang. When the court was convened, Tang had moved to the Public Concession and had not received the summons and did not appear. He also wanted to meet Aizhen and see the children, so he sent a letter to Zou's lawyer asking for her address, but he did not receive a reply. Now, it has been learned that Aizhen has moved from Zhonghua Road to 1269 Lafayette Road. Tang does not know who the house belongs to and is not in a position to visit casually. However, because Aizhen had previously committed adultery and then falsely accused him, their relationship is over, and it is impossible for them to be husband and wife again. Tang is willing to sacrifice all the property he has left with Aizhen, but only asks to be granted a divorce to relieve his mental pain. Aizhen has another love, so it will be difficult for her to fulfill her maternal duties to the two children, and she should also be asked to hand them over to Tang for guardianship. Both parties want a divorce, and the goal seems to be the same, but they have filed lawsuits in two courts, and the jurisdiction is questionable. It is expected that there will be a debate on this issue when the court opens in the future.

Children's Hygiene Movement 186

Grand Situation on the Second Day in Yangshupu

Yesterday (the 24th) was the last day of the children's hygiene movement held by the Chinese Child Welfare Association in Yangshupu, Shanghai. The details are recorded below:
