From 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, a children's health competition was held. Doctors Dong Wenshou (董文壽), Yang Suzhen (楊素珍), Doctor Xu, and Ms. Chen Demei (陳德美) examined the children's physical condition. A total of 164 children participated in the competition. The results of the competition will be announced and prizes will be awarded after comparison and research after the closing of the meeting.

Children's Bathing 188

From 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, Mrs. Hua Jingzhen (華靜貞), Mrs. Pan Shilin (潘石麟), Ms. Wang Aitian (王愛田), and Ms. Hua Meijie (華美傑) presided over the free bathing of children. A total of 196 children were bathed.

Smallpox Vaccination for Children 189

From 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM, doctors Hua Ci (R.G. Watts) and Chu Shenfa (儲伸發) sent by the Public Concession Health Department vaccinated children at the venue. A total of 134 children were vaccinated.

Free Injections 190

From 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, doctors Li Anbang (李安邦) and Shen Zhicheng (沈志澄) sent by the City Health Bureau gave preventive injections to children and adults at the venue. A total of 125 children and 173 adults were injected, for a total of 298 people.

Fly-Swatting Competition 191

In order to eradicate disease vectors, the association launched a fly-swatting competition for primary school students. More than 120 people have registered. The regulations are listed below: (1) The number of participants is limited to 20 per group and 100 per individual. (2) The competition results will be announced daily in two categories: group and individual. (3) Each participant will be given a number (coded on the fly bag), a fly swatter, and a pair of fly chopsticks. Everyone should use and store them carefully. (3) Return them when the competition is over. (4) The minimum number of flies to be submitted for the first time is 100. After that, the number of flies submitted every day at 9:00 AM is unlimited. (5) The fly-swatting period is from June 24 to June 30. (6) Prizes will be awarded to the winners. Three prizes will be awarded to the group and ten prizes to the individual. Honorary awards will also be given to groups and individuals whose scores are not much different from the winners.

Cooperative Stores 192

The association has launched a children's hygiene movement in Yangshupu, Shanghai, and has been greatly encouraged by various major stores that have voluntarily joined the exhibition and implemented cooperation. Among them, companies such as Ke Fa Pharmacy, Sanyou Industrial Society, Palm Olive Soap Company, Quaker Oats Biscuit Company, Angora Condensed Milk Company, Ke Ning Milk Powder Company, Mrs. Winslow's Soothing Syrup, and Twin Swords Brand Antiseptic Water Company have given prizes to the children participating in the health competition to show their promotion and their enthusiasm is particularly commendable.

Pudong Will Have Tap Water 193

Water Plant...Under Preparation

Artesian Well...Under Construction

The Laiyidu area of Pudong is gradually developing, and the residents' drinking water is either transported from the Huangpu River or drawn from the soil wells, which is unsanitary and often causes epidemics. In view of this, the municipal government has ordered the municipal public works bureau to prepare a tap water plant with funds of more than 200,000 yuan. It has been reported that the bureau has surveyed the area of Taoyuan Residence on Youlong Road, Laiyidu, as the site of the plant and is currently acquiring private land for construction. However, the construction of the water plant will take at least one year. In order to respond to the urgent need, the bureau has also submitted a request to the municipal government to first drill an artesian well on the vacant land opposite No. 106 Laiyidu Main Street. The project has been contracted to the Tianyuan Machine Drilling Bureau for 2,600 yuan, and a license has been issued for construction to begin. For the water plant, it is planned to first build a water tower, which has also been priced separately by various manufacturers, so that when the well drilling project is completed in the future, the well water can be pumped into the tower first and then sent to users to supply water.

The Municipal Public Works Bureau Reissues Vehicle and Boat Licenses 194

Small Cars...Cargo Ships...Rowboats, Etc.

New Licenses Must Be Obtained from July 1

The 20-year small car licenses previously issued by the Municipal Public Works Bureau, the validity period of which ends at the end of June of this year, were announced yesterday. All small car owners should, from July 1, take their old licenses to the nearby vehicle affairs offices, pay a license replacement fee of 2 jiao of silver, and receive a new license (valid from July 20 to June 21). In addition, the validity period of the 19th-year licenses for cargo ships and rowboats in the city will also expire on June 30 of this year. The bureau has also issued a notice on the license replacement methods, which are copied below: (1) From July 1 to July 31 of this year, ship owners should take their old licenses to the ship affairs offices where they originally obtained their licenses to replace them with new licenses. (2) A license fee should be paid for obtaining a new license: 3 jiao of silver for each cargo ship and 2 jiao for each rowboat. (3) Ships that have already left the country should wait until they return to the country and retrieve their licenses before being issued new licenses. (4) Starting in July of this year, monthly donations will be paid based on the new license.

Tanjiadu in Wusong River Illegally Increases Ferry Fees 198

Ferry Fees Confiscated...Additional Fine Levied

Liu Shiqi (劉士琦), the ferry operator of Tanjiadu in the Wusong River, had previously been approved by the Municipal Public Works Bureau to increase the ferry fee from one copper coin to two copper coins per passenger. However, from February 10 of this year, he illegally increased the fee to four copper coins per passenger. The local residents then reported to the Public Works Bureau, requesting severe punishment. The bureau sent personnel to investigate and found that the ferry operator was ignoring orders and increasing the burden on the public, which was hateful. With the approval of the municipal government, the ferry operator was ordered to confiscate all the illegally increased ferry fees from February 10 to May 21, calculated at 15,000 copper coins per day, for a total of 515 yuan, and to pay an additional fine of 50 yuan, which will be submitted to the bureau and transferred to the municipal treasury as a warning to others.

The Municipal Public Works Bureau found that the Minghua Water Pipe Engineering Company had repeatedly undertaken water supply equipment installations in new buildings in the First District of the Public Security Bureau and the aircraft manufacturing plant in the Jiangnan Shipyard without first reporting to the Inland Water Company for water connection, which was a violation. In addition, the use of cardboard instead of rubber for the water pipe joint fasteners was even more inappropriate. Furthermore, the owner of the store, Yang Yaonan (楊耀南), was working at the Shanghai Water Company and had no time to take care of the store's affairs, allowing employees to work illegally outside, causing endless harm. During this period, the company is not allowed to operate in the city. The company has now complied.

Reasons for Delay of Pinghu Ferry 200

Due to Mutiny of the Xincang Local Defense Corps

The early ferries running between Pinghu and Shanghai, according to regulations, should have departed from Pinghu at 7:00 AM yesterday (the 24th) - the Shanghai-Pinghu company's ferry, and at 9:00 AM - the Minnan company's ferry. However, neither ferry had arrived in Shanghai by those times. The two companies were worried about accidents along the way and were about to call Pinghu to inquire. Just then, the Shanghai-Pinghu company received a telegram from the Pinghu company reporting that yesterday (the 23rd), in Xincang Town, about two miles from Pinghu, a mutiny of the local defense corps occurred, with approximately four to five hundred people. They wantonly looted and harassed, and most fled via the Zhapu sea route, while a small part scattered. The authorities, in order to search for the mutinous soldiers, ordered the ferries to temporarily suspend operations. It was said that the two Pinghu ferries were scheduled to depart for Shanghai simultaneously at 11:00 AM. Later, in the afternoon, the ferries of the two companies arrived in Shanghai simultaneously. According to passengers, the delayed departure was due to the Xincang mutiny.

Failed Robbery Disguised as Holiday Gift-Giving 201

Female Thief Confesses Details

Male Thief Ding Amao Also Arrested

At Hu Baoli's residence, number 23, Third Tai Wharf, South City, in February of this year, a group of bandits suddenly arrived. Among them was a woman who, under the pretext of delivering a holiday gift, attempted to enter and rob the house, but failed. The detectives of the First District Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau discovered that the female thief in this case was named Zhao Xiaomei, and she was currently hiding in a small inn on Baochang Road in the French Concession. They went to the address the day before yesterday and arrested the female thief Zhao Xiaomei. During the preliminary interrogation, Zhao Xiaomei, also known as Hainü, confessed that she was 29 years old, from Zhenjiang, and previously lived at the Youche Wharf in the South City. In October of last year, she met Ding Amao, who lived in Xuejiabang in the South City, on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. Later, as they were attracted to each other, they stayed together for several nights in the Changfa Inn. Amao had many friends he knew outside, including one named A Lin, who lived near Xieqiao outside the West Gate, and a short man with the surname Zhang who lived in Pudong. These two often came to the inn to play. Around December of the lunar calendar last year, they moved to the Tianfa Inn. A man surnamed Wu, with pockmarks on his face, came to the inn with an unfamiliar person. Wu suggested that as the end of the year was approaching, they were burdened with debts and needed to find a way to get through it. He said that he had learned that Hu Baoli's family at Third Tai Wharf had considerable savings, and they might as well go there together to do some "business" to find a way out. Everyone agreed at the time. So, at about 2:00 PM on the 24th of that month (i.e., in February of this year), they gathered at the 16th Pier in the South City. There were seven people, including Zhao, Amao, Wu Mapi, and Big Head. Because Amao knew too many people in the South City, he did not go with them. Wu Pima wore a short blue cloth shirt, tied a cloth apron around his waist, and carried two pistols. At that time, Zhao first bought a basket of oranges at a fruit shop for one yuan and a box of sponge cakes at a candy store for four jiao and took them to Hu's house. Unexpectedly, after entering, just as they were about to start, they were suddenly discovered, so in a hurry, they threw the oranges and cakes into Hu's courtyard, then exited the gate and ran away

Page 16

They fled to Dongjiadu and took a car back to the inn. They then went to the address to arrest Ding Amao. He confessed that he was 31 years old, from Ningbo, and worked as a tea boy on the Xinjiangtian steamboat. His testimony was the same as Zhao Xiaomei's. Because the case involved robbery, they were ordered to prepare documents and transfer them to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Trial of the Ren Zhennan Fraud Case 202

In the case of lawyer Ren Zhennan, who was accused of fraud by Zhuang Chunpu, the local court filed a public prosecution. Ren hired lawyers Jin Yu and Xue Jiaqi for defense. When Zhuang Chunpu was accused of bigamy by his mistress Wang Lianxiang in the French court and entrusted the defendant, it was stipulated that the public fees were two hundred taels of silver, and it was stated that there would be no other additional demands. The defendant made defenses and appeared in court several times, but Zhuang did not appear in court. It was the fourth court hearing, and Zhuang did not appear in court several times. Zhuang hesitated at first, and the defendant strongly advised him because of the court's prestige. He reluctantly appeared in court and was ordered to pay a bail of 20,000 yuan and be held in custody without bail. His wife, Zhuang Li, blamed the defendant for not having urged her husband to appear in court beforehand and demanded a refund of the public fee, which was refused. A week later, she pleaded with the court to reduce the bail to 10,000 taels. After leaving the court, Zhuang Li pressed the defendant to find a guarantor, but he had no such responsibility and refused. A few days later, she invited hooligans to the office to make trouble, demanding 5,000 yuan in compensation for reputational damage, threatening that they could take people away and bring them back. They reported to the police before leaving. The witnesses she cited, Qian Yumin and others, were her relatives and could not have the value of witnesses. A check for 500 yuan borrowed from Han Tianmin and described by Qian Yumin was a Shanghai Bank check, but the investigation court inquired with Shanghai Bank and found no account names related to anyone in this case, which was obviously a lie. They requested to be found innocent. The case was handled by Judge Qian Chengjun of the Criminal Court. He immediately subpoenaed and opened the fifth court hearing at 2:00 PM yesterday. The official asked Ren Zhennan, who confessed that he was 24 years old, from Guangdong, lived at 16 Beile Road, graduated from Aurora University, returned from studying in France, and registered as a lawyer in June of last year. He asked if he knew Zhuang Chunpu and Zhuang Li. He answered that he did not know them before. He asked who came to ask for a lawsuit. He answered that Qian Yumin asked Gu Gongda to ask for it. He asked what was the matter. He answered that a mistress Wang Lianxiang hired lawyer Zheng Yuxiu to sue for bigamy in the French court. He had already hired lawyer Fei Xizhen and asked me to appear in court. The public fee was 200 taels. He asked if there was another 500 taels of public fee. He answered no. He asked if there was a settlement of 4,500 yuan. He answered no. He asked where the 200 taels were paid. He answered that there was a receipt in the office. He appeared in court twice in February, once in March, and recently once. He asked which day Zhuang Chunpu was detained. He answered the third court. He asked why he was suing him. He answered that because he did not appear in court twice, and the third time he was persuaded to go to court and was detained, he resented me and framed me. At this point, he asked Zhuang Li, who confessed that she was 40 years old, from Ningbo, her husband Zhuang Chunpu was a land broker, lived at 10 Guangyuli, Qialu Road, and Wang Lianxiang was his mistress. He asked if they were still mistresses. She answered no. Later, she filed a lawsuit in court. He asked what she accused him of. She answered abuse. He asked what else. She answered that she didn't know. He asked how she knew Ren Zhennan. She answered that Qian Yumin and Gu Gongda introduced her. He asked which day. She answered February 9. He asked where. She answered the China Hotel. He asked why she didn't go to the office to hire a lawyer, but went to the hotel. She answered that Qian Yumin saw Ren Zhennan in the China Hotel on the 10th. Her husband, herself, Qian, and Gu were all present. Gu said the lawyer could settle the matter, so on February 12, he first paid 500 taels, then 1,000 yuan in banknotes for the first time, 3,000 yuan in banknotes for the second time, and a 500 yuan check for the third time, totaling 4,500 yuan. He asked what it was for. She answered that it was said that lawyer Zheng wanted 4,500 yuan for settlement fees. He asked where the money came from. She answered that it was borrowed from friends, pawned, and mortgaged. He asked if the third payment was a Shanghai Bank check. She answered yes, it was borrowed from Qian Yumin. He asked why she wanted to go to the Ningbo Fellow Association to sue. She answered that she was afraid her husband would be detained. He asked when her husband was detained. She answered February 13 of the lunar calendar. The official said that today's case was slightly inquired about, and a further trial will be conducted for verification. He ordered both parties to leave.

Detective Team Captures Nine Bandits 203

Municipal Public Security Bureau detectives Jiang Jinxiang, Zhang Jinzhou, Han Jingxiang, Zhang Shaoming, Wang Zian, Gao Zihua, Zhang Yingpin, Wu Zuowen, Ning detective Zhang Ruizhi, Zhao Huai'en, Zhang Mingxiang, female detective Xia Xiuying, etc., were inspecting pedestrians in the 16th Pier area at about 10:00 AM yesterday. When they checked near the entrance of Tie Mao Nong, they suddenly noticed more than ten burly men sitting in the Tianbao Garden teahouse, gathered around a table drinking tea. When they saw the detectives, they all looked flustered, and their behavior became more suspicious. The detectives rushed in and checked them. No prohibited items were found on the people present. Finally, a loaded pistol, seven bullets, and a magazine were suddenly found on the stool where one person was sitting. They arrested the men, totaling nine, and immediately took them back to the team. Captain Lu interrogated them one by one. The person carrying the pistol confessed that his name was Liu Zijin, and the others confessed that their names were Li Chunhe, Wang Xiaosizi, Yang Yougen, Chen Yongyuan, Wang Changzhen, Su Chaojiang, Zhu Jifu, and Liu Wanfu. Among them, Liu Zijin, Li Chunhe, and Wang Xiaosizi directly admitted that they were invited by their accomplice Kong Laosi to rob the piglet merchants coming to Shanghai from Jiang'an. After Captain Lu obtained the confession, he ordered the original detectives to step up the pursuit of Kong Laosi, the leader. He also submitted the situation to Director Chen, who praised the team leader for his effective leadership in repeatedly solving kidnapping and robbery cases in recent days, in order to encourage them in the future.

Demolition of the Tall Flagpole in the Temple of the Queen of Heaven 204

In the Temple of the Queen of Heaven on North Henan Road in this city, there used to be a pair of tall flagpoles. Now, due to years of decay, the whole body is shaking, and it is about to destroy houses and injure people. The Third District Party Department of this city believes that these flagpoles are remnants of the feudal system, and they are fundamentally shaking. Demolition is necessary to eliminate bad habits and ensure safety. Therefore, on the 15th of last month, they submitted a report to the Municipal Executive Committee, which forwarded it to the Municipal Government for demolition. Then, the Municipal Government and the Municipal Public Works Bureau jointly sent personnel to the temple to inspect and also agreed that it should be demolished. Therefore, on the morning of the day before yesterday (the 22nd), they sent personnel to lead craftsmen to demolish the flagpole.

Conviction for Forced Confession of Theft 205

Xu Yougen, a cook at Tongchang Restaurant at 423 Zhabu Road, suddenly wore new shoes and socks. When he delivered food to the Central Leather Shoe Store on North Sichuan Road, the store owner found 57 yuan missing from the drawer of the account table. During a strict investigation, he saw that Xu's shoes and socks were new and suspected that Xu had stolen the money. He threatened him to a secluded place, used private torture, and forced him to write a confession of theft. Afterwards, Xu filed a complaint through his employer to the police station, who arrested the shoe store owner Zhang Sansan and the accomplices Shen Hehai, Zhu Axiao, and the suspect Zhou Qifa, and sent them to the Special District Local Court. The fortune teller who wrote the confession was summoned to testify. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng opened the court and sentenced Shen Hehai to eight months in prison, Zhu Axiao to six months in prison, and the confession was confiscated. Zhang and Zhou were acquitted and released.

Important Talk by Yu Hongjun 206

The Income and Expenditure for the 19th Year Can Be Roughly Offset

The Municipal Government Holds a Cautious Principle for Building Bridges over the Huangpu River

Yesterday, a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency interviewed Mr. Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, regarding the final accounts for the 19th year, the budget for the 20th year, and various issues concerning the Huangpu River and bridge construction. According to his talk, as follows:

Final Accounts and Budget 207

According to the talk, the final accounts for the 19th year will be compiled at the end of this month after the accounts from all parties are gathered. It is estimated that it will take about a month to complete. As for the total amount of income and expenditure, according to the budget for the 18th year, the total income of the city is about 7 million yuan, and the expenditure is about 6.5 million yuan. However, in fact, since the Municipal Government has reorganized various tax revenues, the income has exceeded the budget for the 18th year. However, the expenditure also cannot but exceed the budget of 6.5 million yuan due to the increase in prices of all construction materials and temporary payments, etc. However, the comparison of the two items of income and expenditure is roughly offset, with little profit or loss. As for the budget for the 20th year, it is now being submitted to the Executive Yuan for review. It is expected that the income for the 20th year will again… the amount can reach about 8 million yuan. On the expenditure side, it must be determined after the Executive Yuan approves it. The saying that the budget income for the 20th year is more than 6.5 million yuan and the expenditure is more than 7.6 million yuan is completely inaccurate.

Huangpu Bridge Construction 208

Regarding the construction of a bridge over the Huangpu River, the sponsors have repeatedly requested approval from the Municipal Government. Recently, they have also sent draft contracts for review. But in principle, the government should support the people's initiation of bridge construction. However, whether there is a need to build a bridge over the Huangpu River, the financial resources for bridge construction, and whether the soil on the east and west banks is suitable for bridge construction are all very important. Moreover, the Municipal Public Works Bureau's ferry system has gradually become complete. Whether it is really necessary to build another bridge, the Municipal Government has always held a cautious principle on this issue. In addition to sending personnel for detailed investigation, whether to approve it will be submitted to the Municipal Affairs Conference for detailed discussion and decision within days.

Silk Industry Hopes for Early Issuance of Public Bonds 209

Although the 8 million yuan Jiangsu-Zhejiang silk industry public bond has been promulgated and implemented, it has been delayed due to unresolved distribution issues. Silk factories generally believe that this public bond is issued to rescue the silk industry. Now that the actual benefits of the rescue have not been obtained, and the factories have already exported, the Jianghai Customs has levied a special tax of 30 yuan per dan from the 20th of last month to be allocated to the public bond fund. In that case, the factories have suffered harm before receiving benefits. As the new silk is on the market, the work of each factory should be intensified. Now, due to the lack of both funds and raw materials, they have been suspended one after another. Last time, when the spring cocoons were on the market, the public bonds could not meet the urgent needs. Now that the summer cocoons in Zhejiang are about to be launched, there is still no definite date for the issuance of public bonds. Therefore, there is widespread resentment. The other day, the manufacturers all questioned Chairman Shen of the Shanghai Silk Factory Association, leaving Shen speechless. While they were questioning, they suddenly received a notice from the Special Committee for Relief Public Bonds, stating that the Fifth Committee Meeting would be held on the 29th of this month (i.e., Monday) at the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to discuss the fundamental solution for public bonds. Chairman Shen promised to discuss the matter with the members at the due date and issue the bonds earlier.

Sichuan Fellow Association Opposes Post-War Public Bonds 210

Petitioning the National Government to Reject the Requests of Liu Xiang and Others

The Sichuan Fellow Association in Shanghai recently stated that the Sichuan Post-War Supervisor Liu Xiang requested to issue 20 million yuan of Sichuan Post-War Public Bonds, and the Sichuan Provincial Government Chairman Liu Wenhui requested to issue 20 million yuan of Sichuan Provincial Public Bonds, which the people could not afford. They raised objections. On the one hand, they petitioned the National Government to reject the requests of the two Lius. On the other hand, they telegraphed the two Lius, asking them to withdraw the concluded agreement, and telegraphed all agencies, organizations, and Sichuan fellow associations abroad to oppose it. The reasons are as follows: (1) Sichuan has suffered severe disasters in recent years, and commerce has also been depressed. People are displaced and suffering, and they cannot afford this heavy public debt. (2) Although the two Lius claim that the issuance of public bonds is for post-war reconstruction, in fact, there is no legitimate use, but to create civil wars in Sichuan, and the people have no obligation to bear it. (3) The two Lius have the most defense zones in Sichuan and have plundered a lot. Since they do not reduce tariffs and raise funds freely, the military and political expenses are not insufficient. Why do they still need to issue public bonds? (4) The stamp tax and tobacco and alcohol tax raised are used to offset the public bond fund. In fact, the tax revenue in the defense zone of the two Lius is not much, and it has already been used as a pledge when borrowing from the people. The fund is not much. (5) If the public bonds requested by the two Lius are approved, the Sichuan armies will inevitably follow the example. If the central government does not approve, they will also issue them freely, and the people will be unbearable. The full text is more than two thousand words, and the narration is very detailed.

The Truth about the Merger of the Zhaoshang Bureau Navigation School 215

Talk by Secretary Bao Gongfan

Recently, it was heard that the Navigation School run by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was to be merged into the Wusong Merchant Marine School. The students of the school were quite alarmed and had a school protection movement. A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency went to the Bureau yesterday to visit Secretary Bao Gongfan. According to his talk, the content of this matter is quite detailed. The summary is recorded as follows: Wei Jun said that when Commissioner Guo took office, he had no intention of closing the navigation school. Later, after carefully examining the contents of the school, the academic equipment, and the training of talents, he found that they were not very complete, and it was not registered. The fundamental position was very empty. After the students graduated and went out to serve, whether there would be no difficulty in obtaining a license from the Ministry was still questionable. Therefore, Commissioner Guo, out of consideration for the students' technical training and service prospects, had the intention of merging with the Wusong Merchant Marine School. The navigation students will have to board ships and take on the responsibility of driving, and bear the heavy responsibility of the lives and property of the whole ship. All countries in England and Japan are very serious about running this school and do not allow any shortcomings. In case of rough manufacturing, the students themselves are also very dangerous and not only delay the shipping industry. The Wusong Merchant Marine School was originally run by the old Ministry of Communications of Beiping. Many graduates of the school served in the Bureau, and many have been promoted to shipowners. The achievements are still excellent. In the autumn of the 18th year, the school was restored and was of national nature. The old scale was still there, and the funds were taken from the tonnage tax fees of various shipping companies, so there was no shortage of funds. Therefore, the management was quite perfect. The merger of the Bureau School into the school is the most appropriate. It is very convenient for students' academics and future service and licensing. It is heard that the Bureau has strongly requested a merger in the first session last year. The motivation was due to this. However, the students oppose the merger. The reason is that the students must pay fees uniformly after the merger, and it will be difficult to find a way out in the future. But they do not know that ship service must be based on skills and licenses as a prerequisite. Those who graduate from the Bureau School but are not proficient in skills and have incomplete licenses, even if they want to be cited, are allowed by law. On the contrary, those who graduate from merchant ships and meet the conditions will still be cited and sent to the students of the Bureau for the recruitment of talents. There is no distinction between internal and external barriers. In addition, the problem of following the internship, etc., within a school, there is no reason for two kinds of treatment. Moreover, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is now a state-owned agency, and it is easy to blend in with the Ministry of Communications. The Bureau has already submitted a plan to the National Government for approval. How should it be handled in the future, and it must be decided after the approval is returned. However, Commissioner Guo will definitely plan for the students' aftermath.

Special Report

Fei Tang Report, Volume II (8th Installment) 228

Abstract Translation of Parts Four and Five

The report also mentions the issue between the Municipal Council and the National Government regarding the exercise of the right to collect taxes in the International Settlement, as well as the agreements concluded between the Municipal Council, representing the National Government, for the implementation of the Stamp Tax Ordinance and the Consolidated Tobacco Tax Ordinance in the International Settlement. These two agreements have led to a satisfactory resolution of all long-standing difficulties concerning the collection of taxes. The sole basis for this resolution is the mutual recognition by the National Government and the International Settlement Municipal Council of their legitimate interests. Taxes legally collected by the National Government elsewhere, if they are collected in the International Settlement, should not infringe upon or interfere with the Municipal Council's right to collect taxes under the Land Regulations. The existence of the International Settlement should not prevent the National Government from collecting such taxes in the International Settlement. On the other hand, if the Municipal Council's position in exercising its own taxing powers is not impaired, and its administrative powers in the International Settlement can also be effectively guaranteed, then the issue of applying any tax ordinances to the residents of the International Settlement must be determined by the Municipal Council in consultation with the relevant Chinese authorities. If an agreement is reached to apply such ordinances, then the taxes collected in the International Settlement in accordance with the ordinance should be collected by members of the Municipal Council and not by external agents. The fact that agreements of this nature can be concluded for the two taxes mentioned above seems to indicate that the tax issues that have caused so much difficulty in the past now have a good prospect of being resolved. The following recommendations are made for the future: (1) The functions of the Municipal Council. A. The general and exclusive nature of the International Settlement Municipal Council's administrative powers should be defined in comprehensive and clear terms. B. In addition to the general powers granted by Article 11 of the Land Regulations, which allow the Municipal Council to enact by-laws "to improve the administration and ensure better order," the Municipal Council must also have the power to enact by-laws specifically for the implementation of all or part of Chinese laws and regulations within the International Settlement. However, these laws and regulations may be restricted in accordance with the clear needs of the International Settlement's special circumstances. (2) Approval of the by-laws enacted by the Municipal Council. Organize a new body, including: A. Representatives of the consuls of the countries stationed in Shanghai; and B. Personnel appointed by the Chinese government, to exercise the power to approve by-laws currently vested in the consuls and ministers of treaty powers. This body should consist of six or nine people, with Chinese representatives accounting for at least one-third. The approval by a majority of six or nine people should be the final decision. (3) Cooperation between the Municipal Council and the Chinese government authorities. A. The Municipal Council and the Shanghai Municipal Government should have formal and direct contact. Cooperation between the two sides should be based on mutual recognition and respect for their respective exclusive powers within their jurisdictions. However, with regard to roads outside the boundary, flexible arrangements may be made as needed. For matters of common concern to both regions, both sides should strive to agree on a common policy. B. In addition to the general cooperation referred to above, efforts should also be made by both sides to jointly organize and maintain a number of joint institutions to serve the common interests of both regions, thereby developing closer cooperation. If the French Concession authorities are also willing to support this plan, then all of Shanghai will be under the jurisdiction of a body organized by representatives of the three concerned regions. (4) Collection of taxes. Future issues that arise in the International Settlement from the implementation of Chinese laws and regulations regarding the collection of taxes should be handled in accordance with the reasons mentioned above. The outline of such agreements should be the same as the agreements concluded for the implementation of the Stamp Tax Ordinance and the Consolidated Tobacco Tax Ordinance. Additional comments were then added, providing explanations and examples for the above recommendations. Regarding the second recommendation under the heading of cooperation, further suggestions were made as follows: Closer cooperation among the three administrative regions of Shanghai seems most appropriate in public health matters. It is specifically recommended that a fully equipped isolation hospital be established for infectious diseases and a sanatorium be established for tuberculosis. This facility can also be considered an urgent measure for the common benefit of all of Shanghai. Joint efforts by the authorities in each district to meet this common urgent need will be of great benefit. Any suggestions on this point are only of a hypothetical nature, as the Hospital and Nursing Services Committee organized by the International Settlement Municipal Council is currently under investigation, so this suggestion is even more hypothetical. The hypothetical suggestion that I want to put forward is to find a way to organize a joint hospital committee by representatives of the three districts to establish and maintain isolation hospitals and tuberculosis sanatoriums. The income required by the joint committee should be contributed separately by the districts concerned, in proportion to their tax revenue sources. The initial step in establishing this institution seems to be to first establish a joint advisory committee to study the issue of the need for such hospitals and sanatoriums in all of Shanghai. The joint advisory committee is also organized by representatives of the three districts, and its task is to make recommendations regarding the number, size, and location of the hospitals to be established, and to submit a budget of the required expenses. If the plan proposed by the advisory committee is approved by the authorities concerned, an executive committee can be organized in the same way to act on its behalf. The responsibility of the executive committee is to implement the plan and supervise the established hospitals. Estimating the sources of tax revenue that can be collected in each district as a standard for each district's contribution inevitably involves some difficult issues at this time, as there is no unified valuation system in each district. However, it is not impossible to estimate their approximate numbers as a fairer basis for comparison. Any distribution of economic responsibility, whether based on population or on the number of people treated in each district's hospitals, will result in the amount contributed by each district being proportional to the need and not to the resources. The intention of requiring contributions from the authorities in each district in proportion to their resources is to recognize that districts with greater financial resources should bear the responsibility of assisting districts with less financial resources, and to recognize that resisting the various diseases that this plan seeks to address is for the common benefit of all of Shanghai.

Letters

Respectfully, I recently read the news item "Municipal Chamber of Commerce Mediates Dock Donation Issue" in your newspaper's local news column on the 20th of this month. Some of the details are slightly different from the facts. It was found that the cotton cloth industry wanted to add the dock donation to the out-of-town merchants. When the Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened a meeting on the same day, we stated at the time that in terms of purchasing coarse cloth in large quantities alone, the consolidated tax currently collected is one cent and three li and nine hao per bolt, while the cotton cloth industry charges out-of-town merchants an additional one cent and five li. In addition to the consolidated tax that should be paid, there is a surplus of one li and one hao, while the dock donation is two li and four hao. Therefore, according to the total amount, the cotton cloth industry, in addition to paying the consolidated tax and dock donation on behalf of the out-of-town merchants, still has an unexpected fee of eight li and six hao per bolt. As such, in the item of the dock donation, the out-of-town merchants calculate it according to the customer's rate when purchasing goods. All donation fees should be the responsibility of the cotton cloth industry to pay. Therefore, we made every effort to state this intention at the meeting on the same day, but your newspaper omitted it. It concerns the responsibility of the representatives, and we respectfully request that this letter be published in the letters column. Respectfully addressed to the Shen Bao Newspaper Office, Wang Xinfu, Sun Jiechen, and Ji Chun, representatives of the Andong, Yantai, Harbin, and Longkou out-of-town merchants, June 23rd.

Respectfully, according to Yang Changguo of the Shanghai Branch of the Nanjing Chongshan Hall, the news item "Chongdaotang Frauds Money with Ghosts and Spirits" published in your newspaper's local news column on the 21st of this month, the reported situation does not match the facts. It was found that Chongdaotang's main hall is located in Nanjing and is dedicated to abstaining from opium, treating illnesses, distributing clothes and rice, and providing general relief to the people. It is purely a charitable organization that has been investigated and approved by the Nanjing Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and registered, and has been issued License No. Yi 62 on file. In order to promote good deeds, the main hall has set up a branch hall in Shanghai, which has been approved and registered with a license issued by the main hall, License No. Yi 62 on file. The branch hall is subject to the jurisdiction of the main organization. Therefore, in order to avoid any misunderstandings, the branch hall reported to the Municipal People's Training Association for approval and registration, and at the same time, is proceeding with the registration procedures with the Social Affairs Bureau. Among those who have given up opium addiction in the hall, three or four hundred people have succeeded and left happily in the past two years. If there were any fraudulent activities, it would not be allowed by society, and the victims would never remain silent. The facts are all there and cannot be concealed with a few words. As for the people who give up opium addiction, it is only natural that they are grateful and willing to donate to promote their cause because they have gotten rid of their old illness. This is true for all charitable organizations. It is inaccurate to refer to it as fraudulently taking money. Although a police officer from the first precinct of the Public Security Bureau came to inquire about the situation the day before yesterday, he was informed of the details and shown the registration certificate, and he was immediately relieved. There was no mention of ghosts and spirits possessing people or punishing people. It must be inaccurate hearsay. You are requested to send a letter on our behalf to correct it in order to clarify the truth, etc. Special delivery, respectfully request your newspaper to publish it in the news column to correct it. Thank you very much. Respectfully addressed to the editor, Lawyer Yang Changchi, June 24th, 20th year [of the Republic].

Free Talk

A Word or Two 229

— Yi Mei

Court historians: the prison of scholars. Hand bracelets and earrings: the shackles of women.

Fame and money are like fish and bear's paw. You can't have both. But why do people prefer to give up fame and take money?

Optimists and pessimists, although they wear the same sky and tread the same earth, the optimist's world is wide, and the pessimist's world is narrow.

Arguing with people in anger, if you lose, people will laugh at you; if you win, you will laugh at people. Therefore, rather than arguing and then laughing, it is better to laugh first and stop arguing.

Civil war is one of the most shameful pages in the history of warfare.

The whole world blames Zhao, no need to continue writing Supplements to the Records of Spirits. The big cities have many thieves, I cannot bear to re-read Water Margin.

Looking down on others is a great taboo in dealing with the world. Having no self in your heart is serving the public selflessly.

Women are accustomed to using powder and rouge to decorate their ugliness, and scholars are good at using writing to cover up their faults.

If there are mountains to escape to, then escape to the mountains. If there are cities to hide in, then hide in the cities. Both are still considered lofty people.

Roses are not considered to be bad flowers because of their many thorns. Shad is not considered to be bad food because of its many bones.

During the plum rain season, the foundations are moist and about to flow. Living in a closed room is most comfortable.

The evils of the world mostly come from the infatuation with wealth and sex.

Burning a censer of incense, you can read paintings, play the qin, talk about Zen, or sit quietly.

I like to study Buddhism, but I do not like the evening chants and morning bells of the monks, only seeking formality.

In ancient times, those who did not know "rich brocade and fragrant silk" were poor women. In this world, those who do not know "rich brocade and fragrant silk" are models.

The innocent smiles of children are the most adorable.

If there is nothing in the room, getting a painting is enough to comfort the mind. If there is no literary talent in the chest, making a witty remark can also be passed down through the ages.

A Picture of Displaced Refugees 230

— Huai Bing

In the areas of Henan and Hubei, the scourge of bandits is spreading. Wherever the flames of war pass, the fields are in ruins. The misery of the looting is no less than that in southern Jiangxi. The common people have no harvest and cannot fill their stomachs, so they have no choice but to seek relief by begging outside the province. Infants are carried in baskets, and entire villages travel together. The elderly carry burdens on the road, begging for food to prolong their lives. These are called refugees. Between towns and villages, there are often such refugees passing through. Although the provincial government's proclamations are grand, they are not allowed to enter the province. However, the arrival of refugees continues unabated. When officials encounter refugees, they can only follow the usual practice of providing assistance and forcefully preventing them from crossing the border. The supply requires about two or thirty yuan per hundred people. The amount is negotiated and determined by the representatives with the local authorities, as if pricing. Although the matter is troublesome, there is no other good way to deal with it. One day, more refugees arrived in Weiting Town. Out of curiosity, I went to see their situation. There were about seventy or eighty people, all from Si County, Henan, and came from Kunshan. They were about to go west. They were stationed in the east of the town, some emaciated, some with plump complexions. The rich and poor among them were very different. At the time, they were supporting mats as huts and picking up bricks to make stoves, planning a short stay. The rice straw purchased and stored by the Public Security Bureau was looted. There was nothing they could do. If the supply was not satisfactory, there was always the danger of accidents. Among them were three or five people wearing serge robes and superior felt hats, with glittering rings, who were the leaders of the team. Their clothes were quite luxurious. They were addicted to cigarettes and alcohol. The pits of jujubes and the shells of longans were scattered all over the ground. At the time, I saw them cooking eels, without removing the intestines, frying the whole strips in oil. After they were cooked, they tore them apart and ate them, then the intestines and bones were removed. They said that it was too much trouble for the people of Jiangnan to remove the intestines before eating eels. The poor were full of despair and looked forward to receiving food to fill their stomachs. Their joys and sorrows were not evenly distributed. Some also came out to sell white cloth. The cloth was not like the products of Henan. I could not investigate the source of the cloth in detail. Those who were interested asked about the situation in their hometown. They said that the bandits had repeatedly looted without restraint. Those who could not be exploited were often brutally killed to vent their anger. Therefore, there were those who were separated from their wives and children, and those who were buried in ditches. The misery was unbearable to hear.

Elementary School Speech Contest 231

— Ms. Ye Hua

On June 13th, the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau held a municipal elementary school speech contest at Wuben Girls' Middle School. The contest was presided over by the secretary of the Bureau, Cen Youchang, and assisted by Zhang Yanggao and Wang Jinqi. A large number of male and female guests participated enthusiastically, with fragrant clothes, beautiful hairstyles, and colorful flowers. It was a grand occasion. I will record a few things to remember.

Dressed in Red and Green: The speakers were all about ten years old. Most of the clothes they wore were newly made. Most of the materials were red and green. This is because children's psychology is in line with the primitive peoples, who prefer colors that are bright and eye-catching, as if attending a wedding banquet. Some of the male students wore suits, from ties to leather shoes, which were very exquisite. Mr. Zhang said that a student at a certain university in Japan may not bring his lecture notes and books, but he must have a mirror and shoe-shining cloth. The suits of our country's elementary school students are beautiful and can be compared with those of Japanese university students. However, Japanese university students are old but do not learn, while our country's elementary school students learn but are not old.

Girls Excel: In the end, five winners were selected. Four of these five winners were girls. According to past history, the first place has always been a female student. The linguistic ability of girls seems to be superior to that of boys. The American educator Thorndike investigated the mental differences between the sexes. Girls were better than boys in word cancellation tests, spelling, national language, and foreign languages. From this, the linguistic ability of girls can be seen.

Three Points for Judging: The performance of the speeches has improved more than before. Students such as Shang Wenxi and Cheng, etc. were also very appropriate. In the event of any deficiencies, the judge Lu Feibo provided on-the-spot guidance on one point. (1) A speech is a speech, not just reciting. In the future, remember the main ideas and do not have to stick to the words. Then it will be fluent. (2) Most of the attitudes are unnatural, like acting in a play, like arguing, like Shandong people selling their fists. In the future, there should be movement in stillness and stillness in movement. Strive for liveliness and naturalness, and you can win. (3) There are quite a few people whose accents are not correct. "Shen" is read as "Cheng". "Lv" is read as "Li". "Mo" is made as "Ma". "Sun" is made as "Shen". There are many more. Pay attention at all times and you can improve.

Tidbits 232

— (Du Juan)

The world today is indeed too boring and too dull. Therefore, most pessimistic people want to end their lives by committing suicide and escape to another world. But the boredom and dullness of another world may be even worse than this world. By the time you want to escape back, it will be too late.

Interesting Anecdotes About Arresting Bodhisattvas 233

— Gao Wenqi

Since Mo Runxun became the head of the Public Security Bureau in Shaoxing, our city has been extremely serious about investigating and prohibiting opium, gambling, and prostitution. Moreover, they have been vigorous and exerted every effort in eradicating superstition. Recently, they even arrested Huanglao Xianggong (the most revered deity in Shaoxing) and female shamans who used deities to collect money. Consequently, both "dead" and "living" Bodhisattvas have been arrested. The matter is quite amusing, so I record it as follows:

Bodhisattvas Actually Become Prisoners — The shrines of Huanglao Xianggong in Shaoxing are found everywhere, with those in Qingdian Lake, Jiangjia Lou, and Shiyantou being particularly famous. Every year on Huanglao's birthday, villagers celebrate the deity's birthday with operas and temple fairs, which are extraordinarily lively. Director Mo believes that such superstitious activities not only waste people's money and resources but also easily cause trouble. To fundamentally eliminate these issues, he specially dispatched police to arrest the Huanglao Xianggong idols from the three locations of Qingdian Lake, Jiangjia Lou, and Shiyantou and bring them to the city, temporarily detaining them in the City God Temple. These venerable Bodhisattvas have thus been transformed into prisoners.

Turns Out They Were Gluttonous Bodhisattvas — A woman surnamed Wang from Chang'an Street recently claimed to be possessed by a deity and able to predict good and bad fortune. In her home, she enshrined a red deity tablet inscribed with the absurd and bizarre phrase "The position of the late Mrs. Wu, the stepmother, is continued." Her neighbor, a Mrs. Song, consulted her about her fortune. Mrs. Wang, falsely claiming to speak on behalf of the deity, said that she would die within a hundred days unless she offered five dou of rice, one turtle, and two jin each of dried longan and lotus seeds for the deity to devour. Mrs. Song believed it to be true and immediately gave her the requested items. This matter came to the attention of the Public Security Bureau, which promptly dispatched police to arrest the woman. This gluttonous Bodhisattva did not get to eat the offerings but instead tasted the flavor of a jail cell first.

Bodhisattvas Also Know to Collect Consultation Fees — The wife of a Mr. Xu from Dongpu also falsely claimed to be possessed by a deity and able to cure illnesses. Initially, those who sought treatment only needed to offer a set of incense and candles. Later, as the number of seekers increased, she claimed that the Bodhisattva was now practicing medicine and required a consultation fee of two jiao to show respect. This was subsequently increased to four jiao, and recently, it was increased to one yuan. Her daily income surpassed even that of famous doctors, causing them to sigh with envy. People called her a "living Bodhisattva," and some even sent her inscribed plaques. However, Xu's wife remained greedy and insatiable, and she solicited donations to create a statue for the deity. As a result, she swindled six or seven hundred yuan. A villager named Cai, seeing this, coveted the money and wanted to share the spoils with Xu's wife. Xu's wife refused, so Cai reported her to the police station, accusing her of collecting money under the guise of a deity. Thus, this "living Bodhisattva" who practiced medicine was also arrested and imprisoned. It is said that she will be charged with the crime of obtaining money through fraud.

Travel Notes on India (51) 234

— Linghua

On the 13th, I gave a lecture at the university, chaired by President Amavanatha Tha. The students asked many strange questions, which lasted about two hours. New materials were discovered here regarding the study of war psychology. According to a certain professor, a family of monkeys consists of one male and over ten females. The male monkey is vicious and sometimes kills the female monkeys. This short story is comparable to the Arabian Nights tale of King Shahryar, who took a new wife every night and killed her in the morning. This proves the evils of war, with the male being the root cause. Marx's materialistic view of history is incomplete. Unless male wealth and power are equalized, the world will be difficult to pacify. This is what the biology professor told me. He wanted to oppose my scholarship. Even if men and women cooperate, conflict is unavoidable. However, his example proves the evil of the male. Even if he does not love the female, he kills her after intercourse, which is similar to the example cited by the Englishwoman Felipu of male cats killing their kittens. Both powerfully prove that male physiology is the root of war, which I find increasingly convincing. Monkey nature is considered gentle among animals, yet the evil of the male is such. No wonder in Tokyo, Japan, every morning the newspapers report cases of husbands killing their wives. Thus, the male is indeed the root of war.

On the 14th, I attended a debate at the home of the Muslim scholar Rehmen. Over ten professors and eminent lawyers, all Muslims, participated. The debate lasted a long time. In the end, Lawyer Rehmen was appointed as the organizing committee member. All acknowledged my argument and signed their names. The Muslim author Misrza Shuifaxze presented me with his two books: an English biography of Muhammad and Muhammad's teachings. He hopes that someone in China can translate them. Finding a Quran in Chinese is very difficult. The Muslim bookstore in Ximen, Beijing, does not have one either. The English version costs thirty yuan, which is too expensive. Many English books on Islam are written by Christians, which may not be entirely reliable. In Misrza's biography of Muhammad, his wife Khadija is described as a widow who had been married twice before. She proposed to Muhammad, who was then her third husband. When Muhammad was enlightened, Khadija recognized and publicized his teachings. Khadija was forty years old and Muhammad was twenty-five when they married. After twenty-five years, Khadija died at the age of sixty-five, and Muhammad, at fifty, began to spread his teachings through military force. This proves that the power of Islam came from women. During Khadija's lifetime, military force was not used to spread the religion. Therefore, Islam does not treat women poorly, but its customs resemble those of the Qedarites. The original intention was not to oppress women. Moreover, the custom of polygamy among Muslims in the desert states that Muhammad only married multiple wives after Khadija's death, and even then, it was only a few, compared to the thousands of concubines of Chinese emperors. The Muslims I have met in various places have very modern ideas and strong organizational skills. Their future rise is to be expected and immeasurable. Muslims are more effective than Indians in execution. Indians are fond of talking and fantasizing but are lazy in action. This is their great shortcoming. Muslims, knowing that there are Muslims in China, are particularly friendly to the Chinese.

Fiction: Rotary Club

[P???>

— Xu Zhuodai

Ziliang was somewhat displeased that she was disturbing his sleep while he was sound asleep. He quickly used his right hand to push Yue Ru away and then turned his body in a "left turn" motion, as if on a parade ground. He turned towards the outer bed, pulled the quilt up a little, covered his head, and planned to go back to sleep, knowing that it was still early.

Ziliang's actions managed to keep his wife away for the moment, but who knew that in a short while, his wife had gone to the foot of the bed. His wife lifted the quilt off his feet. Ziliang felt the cold on his feet and retracted his legs. Unexpectedly, he felt a strange itch on the soles of his right foot. He wanted to escape, but his foot was already unable to move, as it had been grabbed by his wife's hand.

At this point, he was very angry. He hurriedly threw off the quilt and sat up:

"What are you doing?"

Ziliang glared and asked his wife, who was giggling. At that moment, his wife had already released his foot and was holding a bed brush in her right hand, covering her mouth with the back of her left hand, laughing non-stop. The bed brush was the one she had just used to brush the soles of his feet.

"Isn't it Sunday today? Can't you let me sleep in a little longer?"

Yue Ru didn't answer, but continued to laugh at Ziliang.

"I didn't go to sleep until after twelve o'clock last night, haven't you thought about that? And you still want to come and fool around!"

As Ziliang spoke, he threw the corner of the quilt that was still on his body towards the inner bed, his face full of anger, towards his wife who was sitting in the middle of the bed. His wife laughed even harder.

"You get up early in the morning and make such a scary face. You're frightening me! You should go to the water basin and take a look at that face of yours!"

Upon hearing this, Ziliang was both annoyed and amused. She usually scolded me for being a stingy ghost, and today she simply told me to go to the water basin and look at my face.

"Other people's husbands are so gentle and pleasant to their wives; only you are making scary faces all day long!"

Yue Ru continued.

"If you don't feel like sleeping, just get up and go downstairs! I want to sleep."

"No! Husband and wife are supposed to share the same bed in life and the same grave in death. Since I've gotten up and am not sharing the same bed with you, you should get up too!"

"Nonsense!"

"Nonsense? There are also walnuts and dates!"

Correction: In the seventh line of the twenty-fourth issue, "section of the neck" should be "back of the neck."

Yarn and Cotton Yarn Market Morning Decline Afternoon Rebound 249

Ultimately, the Summary Is Still Slightly Lower

The yarn market fell in the morning and rebounded in the afternoon, but the trend was relatively calm. Because actual sales were not smooth. However, purchases were very enthusiastic in the past few days. After a large number of transactions, there must be a period of calm. Therefore, although business was slow, the stock was still short in various factories. The spot yarn market was still able to maintain its price. However, the tag yarn was weakened by the short selling of large accounts, which caused the sentiment to weaken, and spot yarn sales were stagnant. Generally, small amounts were frequently showing signs of unease, so the market trend gradually declined. However, according to the actual situation, there should be no such decline. Although the silver price was up, the price of goods had soared. Compared with the two, the price of the spot yarn was still cheap. Therefore, the export trade with Japan was continuous. The Shenxin Factory again sold 800 bales of 16-count and 20-count "Ren Zhong" yarn.

Grain and Rice Market Decline Intensifies

Xinzha 256

Yesterday, the source of goods from various guilds was thirty to forty numbers. Sales were sluggish. The market for Changshu thick japonica rice continued to decline, with Central Gate goods shrinking by about 0.2 tael. The market situation showed a further decline. Thin rice arrivals were weak, and prices fell by 0.1 to 0.2 tael. The outflow of foreign Du Jian rice was limited. River stocks gradually increased, and buying interest was subdued. A small amount of Ba Ba Jian rice arrived, with some separate dismantling. Production news continued to soften, and prices shortened by a fraction. Customer Jian rice was cheaper, so store owners were still eager, but the situation only slightly eased. Foreign rice sales were small, only about a half foot. Trading was not active. White Yuan arrivals were strong daily, and prices fell by 0.1 to 0.2 foot.

Hunan 257

Yesterday, about 30 boats arrived in the Huangpu River. Sales in this street were minimal. The declining trend of thick japonica rice intensified, with a large decline of about 0.2 tael. Foreign Du Jian rice was greatly affected by foreign rice, and sentiment was extremely soft. Because foreign rice goods were similar to Lu Jian rice, sales were scarce, shortening by 0.1 to 0.2 tael. Thin rice such as Qingjiao, Sisong, and Liantang arrived continuously. Inward purchases from all parties were weak, and prices fell with the general trend by 0.2 to 0.3 tael. Early rice sales were brisk, with some trading. The market price must be tired by about one foot. Glutinous rice was sold as it arrived, and the price did not rise or fall.

Flour Market Has Strong Selling Pressure 258

Prices Fall Two Fen in Each Month

Yesterday, the flour market again showed a declining and weak trend. Foreign wheat quotations fell sharply by about 0.6 to 0.7 tael. Domestically, the Xisu guilds had frequently absorbed supplies due to the scarcity of new wheat arrivals. However, this year's wheat harvest varied in quality, so observations differed based on the quality of the harvest. In terms of actual sales, due to the large harvest in the north, they decreased compared to previous years. Yesterday, due to the decline in foreign wheat quotations and the surge in arrivals in Wuxi, prices also weakened. For a time, selling pressure steadily increased, and prices fell for both near and far months. Looking at future trends, with actual sales being very quiet and new wheat arrivals surging, prices will likely fall further. As a result, this month fell by 0.0075 tael compared to the previous day, July fell by 0.015 tael, August fell by 0.0225 tael, and September, October, and November each fell by 0.02 tael.

Wheat Prices Fall as Arrivals Surge 259

Yesterday, in the wheat futures market, due to foreign wheat quotations falling by 0.6 to 0.7 tael, the sentiment of steadfastly holding on to prices could not [be maintained]. Arrivals had reached ten thousand bags, unlike the silence of a few days ago. Because Shanghai factories were mostly watching, only Wuxi factories were selectively buying high-quality goods, so prices also did not increase, tending towards a downward trend. Given this situation, sentiment was weak, and selling was prevalent. Looking ahead, if arrivals from both local and foreign ports continue to surge, prices will likely fall further. As a result, this month fell by 0.03 tael compared to the previous day, July fell by 0.03 tael, August and September fell by 0.05 tael, October fell by 0.04 tael, and November fell by 0.05 tael. In the spot wheat market, because standards weakened and large factories were still watching, the situation for mid-quality goods was very bad. Yesterday, Penglai wheat opened at 3.65 tael, Shuangfeng wheat at 3.75 tael and 3.72 tael. Only Huafeng allocated 1,000 bags.

Silk and Tea Factories Exported to the US Trigger Price Increase 260

Yesterday, in the local foreign silk market, prices suddenly trended upwards. It was found that Japanese silk prices in the New York market had risen sharply in unison. Shanghai white factory silk prices were transferred electronically, not weak, but the increase was not high. Because the costs of Chinese merchants were relatively high, transactions were still difficult to reach smoothly. Yesterday, Qianli and others bought 50 bales of B-grade Shanghai white factory silk, and prices rose sharply by 10 to 20 tael.

Summer Silkworm Development in Yuhang is Delayed 261

After the rainy season, combined with overcast and cold weather... silkworms' molting is uneven.

Farmers in the Pingyao, Changleqiao, and Jinjianong areas of Yuhang are experiencing a good summer silkworm rearing season this year. Unfortunately, due to the difficulty of purchasing silkworm eggs and the prevalence of mixed breeds, the hatching was not easy. After receiving the silkworms, the weather was sunny and warm, and everything went well. However, after the third molt, there were continuous rainy days, and the weather suddenly became cold and hot, causing changes in the silkworms. Some were abandoned. Although it is sunny now, it is still overcast and cold, and the silkworms' development is delayed. The early batches have entered the major molt, and molting is uneven.

Qining Fragrant Tea Sales to Russia Improve 262

Yesterday, in the local foreign tea market, interest in Qimen and Ningzhou fragrant black tea from Russian Assistance Society foreign firms continued to grow. The total trading volume was over 2,100 boxes, and transactions were quite brisk. However, due to the severe prices in the future, the market price had shrunk to 18-19 tael, a further drop of 4-5 tael compared to before. The market situation for Luxhuang Zhenmei green tea remained desolate. Zhongguan goods such as Baochang and Tongfu slightly increased their inventory. Chinese merchants were still mostly unwilling to relax on tea with better production methods. However, in terms of the overall tea market trend, the green tea market has already shown an unfavorable trend.

Japanese Sugar Slightly Firms After Falling

Yesterday, sugar market telegrams stated that the current Cuban sugar price was still 1.34375, the New York futures price for September was 1.31, and the price for December was 1.40. Piece Goods and Gold Markets Plunge, Prices Turn Downward

Local Factory Cloth 264

Yesterday, the market saw mixed rises and falls. Light-weight coarse cloth was quite strong due to the lack of spot goods. 11-pound Three Deer rose to 5.675 tael, Ren Zhong to 5.45 tael, and 9-pound cloth uniformly went out of customs at 5 tael. Mao Ying had to be 5.15 tael, and Wufu 5.1 tael. Ningbo and Wenzhou guilds were quite active in purchasing. Fine cloth plunged due to the plunge in the gold market, and the northern guilds' inward demand turned stagnant, so it had already turned from rising to falling. Blue Chicken was 7.575 tael, Color Ball was 7.75 tael, Yanghe was 7.7 tael, and Blue Double Fish was 7.75 tael. Yesterday, only sporadic additions were made in this street. Fine twill was still stable.

Eastern and Western Piece Goods 265

The market situation was greatly affected by the ups and downs of the gold market. The guilds of Tianjin, Sichuan, Changsha, etc., which were unusually active before, have now uniformly taken a wait-and-see attitude. This street has had little purchasing recently, resulting in a sudden drop in actual sales and a weakening of sentiment. Fortunately, the continuous rise of Sanpin has kept prices in check. Yesterday, Zhigong woolen cloth all slightly fell, with Moganshan Lieyan and others at 0.38 tael, Sanyou Tu at 0.345 tael. Fine bombazine fell more sharply at Huxinting, with a small decline of about 0.0075 tael. Yuanyang yarn also followed its decline. Dianqiuxiang, Shuangtonglu, and Hanshansi all fell by 0.025 tael. Only fine cloth and bleached cloth rose.

North-South Goods, New Guangdong Branches Are Expensive and Not Yet Open 266

The lotus bag branches produced in Guangdong have been harvested somewhat this year, but due to the small quantity, the purchasing price is very high. Yesterday, the Beishi merchants rushed to transport four boxes, which were already shown as samples. The color was good, but the sweetness was inferior. It was heard that the cost must be 45-46 tael. Because the counteroffer from the traders was too far off, no deal has been made yet.

Metals, Garden Galvanized Wire Imported in a Steady Stream 267

Since the ordnance factories and military supply offices purchased garden galvanized wire last week, the local stock has been depleted. The standard rose sharply by 0.07-0.08 tael, and the highest price per bundle was estimated at 5.75 tael. However, local industry insiders, seeing that the source of Western goods was not being followed up, have switched to handling Eastern goods, so the import of Eastern garden galvanized wire is incessant. It is heard that over the last three days, arrivals have reached as many as 5-6,000 bundles, and subsequent shipments continue to arrive, so spot goods in the market may have a surplus in the future.

Another 300 Tons of Ribbed Steel Bars Arrive 268

Recently, due to oversupply, the market for ribbed steel bars has been weak. The standard is only estimated at 95 tael per ton, a successive decline of 2-3 tael compared to before. But the large number of arrivals has caused the market to decline further. Yesterday, Western warehouses at each port had arrivals of over 300 tons, and the market situation was even more sluggish than before.

1/4-Inch Nails, New Goods Have Arrived 269

There has been a shortage of 1/4-inch nails for many days, so the general purchasers in the market are eagerly awaiting them. The price has risen successively from 13 tael to 14.5 tael. Later buyers have almost been unable to get goods. In the past two days, new goods have arrived from various foreign firms such as Jiecheng, Kong Shimmei, and Zuishi. Therefore, customers who need this product are all elated. It is heard that over 200 barrels were sold on the market yesterday, with prices estimated at 14.25 tael, which is already 0.025 tael cheaper than before.
