Automobile News

Commentary

Establishment of American Highways 286

— Xue Qian

Among the European and American nations, the advancement of their automobile industries is naturally led by the United States. Likewise, the establishment of their highways is most orderly in the United States. For major aspects such as road width, vehicle lanes, the function of signage, and pedestrian convenience, there are definite rules, forming the basis for the neatness of the roads. These are described separately as follows:

Highway Width　American highways have separate regulations for major roads near cities and those connecting large cities. Ordinary roads are only designed for two lanes of traffic. Initially, vehicles were smaller and speeds were lower. Therefore, surveys of road widths showed that those built before 1918 were mostly 16 feet wide, with some as narrow as 14 feet. As automobile manufacturing increased in size and driving speeds increased, highways built after 1920 were mostly standardized at 18 feet. After 1928, the standard was often set at 20 feet. Although these standards vary by state, the specified widths may not be uniform even within a single state. However, the maximum width of a vehicle is generally limited to eight feet. Consequently, curves are often widened, and regulations also exist for highway intersections, widening the road by several feet within 100 or 200 feet to allow for vehicle waiting.

Vehicle Lanes　Ordinary highways with a width of 20 feet or less only have two lanes. Highways between large cities have three or even six lanes. At key locations or corners, black boundary lines are often painted on the road to indicate separation, making it easier for vehicles to identify lanes and avoid collisions.

Overview of Traffic　Traffic is heaviest on American highways in the eastern states. Major roads often see more than 10,000 vehicles per day, with the busiest thoroughfares reaching as many as 25,000 vehicles. The situation is different in the southern states, where traffic is lighter, with daily vehicle counts reaching up to 5,000 at most or as few as 500. Examining the types of vehicles, private passenger cars account for about 90%, while freight and public buses account for only slightly more than 10%. Public passenger vehicles make up only 1% or 2% of the total. This phenomenon is significantly different from Europe, where heavy freight vehicles hold an important position in traffic. However, in the United States, vehicle size is limited to eight feet in width, and each state has its own weight standards, generally limited to the load per inch of rubber tire width, with no fixed limit on the total vehicle load. Therefore, heavy-load vehicles often have three axles, each with four rubber tires. Automobiles traveling on American highways mostly use hollow rubber tires, with solid rubber tires being rare. This is another significant difference from Europe. Furthermore, iron-rimmed rubber tires are rarely seen. Other slow-moving vehicles, such as handcarts and horse-drawn carriages, mostly travel on rural roads, being rarely seen on major highways. Could there be restrictions on human and animal power in traffic regulations?

Intersection Arrangements　The so-called intersection arrangement refers to the arrangement at the intersection of highways and railways. In the past, highways and railways intersected at the same level. Although there were barriers, accidents were countless. Nowadays, highways with heavier traffic often use overpasses or underpasses for railway crossings, considering them more suitable and safer. The costs are generally shared equally. Even at highway intersections, separations are often made, sparing no expense to ensure traffic safety. This is a major recent advancement in the United States. However, most ordinary highways still intersect with railways at the same level, with the hope of gradual improvement in the future.

Signage Function　Signage erected on American highways serves two purposes: indicative and warning. Indicative signs include national highway numbers, provincial highway numbers, distances to cities, left and right turns, and connections to other roads, all using white signs with black text. Warning signs, such as railway crossings, curves, slopes, and school zones, use yellow signs with black text. For special circumstances, such as slippery roads or obstructions, even more conspicuous signs are used. For example, in Shanghai, to prevent vehicle accidents and pedestrian hazards, there are signs that read "Roads are like a tiger's mouth; do not walk in the middle," but there is no fixed format.

Pedestrian Convenience　American highways often have gas stations for refueling, oiling, and air compression. Public facilities provide telephones at reasonable intervals along the route, allowing pedestrians to communicate with friends and family anytime, anywhere. Belgium is the most comprehensive, with a public telephone every kilometer and a pole every 200 meters indicating the distance to the telephone. However, the vastness of the United States may make this difficult to implement. There are also restrooms to facilitate travelers. On the private side, residences along the highway often welcome tourists to stop. Signs are erected in front of homes, and those who wish to dine, lodge, or bathe midway due to lateness will find it convenient. Moreover, small wooden cabins with multiple eaves are built beside the houses, with elevated beds, costing one U.S. dollar per night, creating a home-away-from-home atmosphere, reflecting the emotional nature of the people.

Sharp Increase in French Automobiles 287

— Pei Gan

Recently, a Mr. Teck wrote an article in the New York Times stating that in 1930, France led the world in automobile sales, surpassing even the United States. This development is unprecedented in the automotive industry. According to "American Automobiles" magazine, France's additional car registrations increased by 178,000 units last year, while the United States only increased by 126,094 units. In terms of percentage increase, the progress is even more remarkable, with France increasing by 13.5% and the United States by 0.5%.

The number of new car registrations in twelve countries including France, the United States, and the United Kingdom at the end of 1930 is listed below:

France　　　178,000 units

United States　　126,100 units

Great Britain　　　83,700 units

Germany　　　　　49,700 units

Canada　　　　45,600 units

Italy　　　　28,000 units

Argentina　　　　21,700 units

Belgium　　　　17,700 units

Netherlands　　　　17,000 units

New Zealand　　　　16,000 units

South Africa　　　　14,600 units

Switzerland　　　　14,300 units

France has experienced less economic difficulty than other countries, allowing it to continue its efforts to advance the automotive industry in 1930. Such achievements can only be found in highly affluent and civilized nations. Horses, bicycles, and oxcarts still travel in French cities and villages and occupy an important position. However, the "friend of humanity" powered by gasoline can be seen expanding its influence everywhere.

Currently, there is one car for every 28 people in France, a remarkable record in Europe, but still far behind the United States, where there is one car for every 4.6 people. In Canada and New Zealand, the ratio of people to cars is 7.5 and 10, respectively.

France's current situation is similar to that of the United States in 1917, when there was one car for every 28 people. Some may ask whether the French will have one car per person in another fourteen years. The answer is that it will take a longer time.

Two-thirds of the French population are farmers who are conservative and slow to recognize the benefits of trucks and trailers. Therefore, today's car dealers mostly seek customers in large cities. Paris alone accounts for one-seventh of all cars in France, with one car for every 19 people.

In terms of the total number of cars, France has fewer cars than the United Kingdom. However, this year, French car sales will be second only to the United States. In 1930, France's car sales increased by 95,000 units more than the UK, and if it can increase by 58,000 units in 1931, it will surpass the UK again. The top five countries with the highest car sales are listed below:

January 1930

United States 26,691,000

Great Britain　1,558,000 units

France　　1,500,000 units

Canada　　1,215,000 units

Germany　　　　659,000 units

The tariffs passed by the French Parliament in April 1930 significantly increased taxes on automobiles, greatly impacting U.S. foreign trade. This can be seen in the import and export report of January 2. Domestic production in France decreased by about 20% a year ago, and passenger car exports fell by 12.5% in January and February. Imports accounted for 69.2%.

U.S. importers continue to spend large sums of money in Paris to display car models for public viewing. This is purely for advertising purposes. Ford cars are still assembled in France, and the use of French materials is increasing daily. According to last year's annual report, the new tariffs only increased the cost of Ford cars by 4%, and the retail price remains unchanged.

John Lawrence, the European representative of the National Automobile Chamber of Commerce, has returned to Paris headquarters after a six-week trip to the Baltic states. He examined Germany, Poland, Estonia, Latvia, and Lithuania. Lawrence reported that there are signs of improvement in all areas, contrary to initial observations and expectations. He said, "German manufacturers of automobile parts have increased their work plans for the summer, reversing previous reduction strategies. Demand is improving everywhere."

New Information on Zhejiang-Wuxi Road Administration 289

— Xue Qian

Zhejiang Province Handles Joint Transportation on the Hangzhou-Pinghu Route The Zhejiang Construction Department, noting the increasing development of the province's highway system and the surplus in various road sections, along with the promising traffic conditions, has approved a joint transportation venture between the Provincial Highway Administration and the Hangzhou-Pinghu Road Company to benefit long-distance travelers. The proposed measures have been revised and are now being issued, with instructions for all joint transportation revenue to be reported monthly. The following are ten provisional measures extracted from the joint transportation plan between the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Administration and the Hangzhou-Pinghu Automobile Company for the Hangzhou-Penggongling route: (1) This Administration, to facilitate long-distance travelers between Xiaohe and Hangzhou's Lakeside and Penggongling and Xiaohe, will temporarily provide one passenger car to operate between Xiaohe and the Lakeside, exclusively handling joint transportation with the company at the Xiaohe station. (2) The company will receive the Administration's Xiaohe-Lakeside tickets and luggage tickets for distribution and sale at each station. The Administration will also receive the company's tickets and luggage tickets for each station and the joint transportation tickets between Xiaohe and Penggongling for sale at the Hangzhou station. (3) The Administration and the company will settle ticket revenues every ten days, with each settling in cash and temporarily waiving handling fees. (4) The joint transportation passenger car will operate eight round trips daily, with its schedule aligned with the company's schedule. (5) If the company's schedule changes, it must promptly report to the Administration for revisions. (6) Children between four and ten years old and military police in proper attire and official insignia may purchase half-price tickets. If half-price tickets are sold improperly, the loss must be compensated by the salesperson. (7) Luggage transported through the Xiaohe-Lakeside section must be handled in accordance with the Administration's luggage regulations. (8) The duration of the joint transportation is not fixed and may be canceled at any time if the Administration deems it unnecessary. (9) These measures will take effect on the date of approval by the Construction Department.

Wuxi Changes and Widens City Streets The regulations for widening streets in Wuxi City were previously drafted by the County Construction Bureau, approved by the Construction Department, and submitted to the County Political Conference for revision and adoption for temporary use. They have been announced in newspapers, and the county has submitted them to the Construction Department for approval. Recently, Construction Department Director Sun, finding the regulations still inadequate, specifically instructed the County Government to revise them jointly with the Construction Bureau. The original order stated, "Received and noted. Upon reviewing the submitted regulations and maps for widening city streets, there are still inadequate aspects. The main purpose of widening city streets is to facilitate the majority of pedestrians and accommodate vehicle traffic. Examining the submitted street plan, except for the Guangfu Gate or Chong'an Temple section, which has already been widened, the entire city's routes remain winding, and the maximum width generally does not exceed twelve meters. The main east-west and north-south arteries of the city have frequent pedestrian traffic and should have wide sidewalks to avoid crowding. The width of the sidewalks should be at least one and a half meters, totaling three meters on both sides. With a street width of eight meters, removing three meters leaves only five meters for vehicles, which is insufficient. Furthermore, the ratio of sidewalk width is also inappropriate. It must be understood that widening existing streets should not only consider current needs but also anticipate future needs, achieving a one-time widening to avoid the loss of repeated demolitions. The city's east-west and north-south directions should have one straight through-line in each direction. Obstacles within the routes should be removed during the widening, and the width, including sidewalks, should be twelve meters. Immediately comply with these instructions and direct the County Construction Bureau to revise separately, resubmit them to the County Political Conference for approval, and submit them to the Department for record. Other secondary streets and lanes should be reduced accordingly based on needs. Submit another case for approval."

Recent Conditions of Zhejiang Province's Highways 290

— Fan

Since the establishment of the Highway Bureau in Zhejiang Province, it has spared no effort in planning and implementing road construction and traffic, leading the country's provinces. Here is a brief description of the recent conditions of various roads that have been opened to traffic:

Xiaoshao Section The Xiaoshao section is the origin of provincial roads, built by Lu Zihai when he governed Zhejiang, converting soldiers into laborers. It has been open to traffic for over five years. This section is the eastern part of the Hangzhou-Shaoxing line, starting from the Jiangbian in Xixing and ending at the Five Clouds Gate in Shaoxing. Xiaoshao counties are rich in products and have a large population, with a relatively affluent local lifestyle. With recent improvements over the past two years, business has gradually increased. Currently, the average daily business is approximately 1,300 yuan, making it the leader among all road sections.

Gongsang Section The Gongsang section is the southern part of Hangzhou-Shaoxing, connecting the Xiaoshao section, serving as the central hub of eastern and western Zhejiang and the throat of the Qiantang River Canal. It starts from the Sanlang Temple in Jianggan and ends at the Gongchen Bridge. It opened to traffic in August of the 17th year. After opening, passenger convenience and business developed rapidly. However, in the summer of the 18th year, during the West Lake Expo, ticket holders could ride for free, completely sacrificing the section's business for five months, resulting in vehicle and business losses of over 100,000 yuan. It gradually recovered after reorganization. Recently, it has further developed, with average daily business of approximately 600 yuan. However, the section passes through the central area of Hangzhou, where the essence is concentrated, resulting in many short-distance passengers, but there are too few branch stations, causing public inconvenience. If more branch stations could be established, it would not only develop business but also greatly benefit the public. Currently, the city area is vast, and the public's needs are not limited to this line. There are plans to open new lines and increase vehicles, which will greatly benefit Hangzhou's industrial and commercial enterprises. There is also a branch line to Liuhu, connecting the Lakeside to the Liuhe Pagoda, specifically for tourists, which is more developed in spring and autumn. In addition, there is a movie special bus, set up to facilitate power plant users to watch movies.

Hangchang Road Hangchang Road is a national highway between Beijing and Hangzhou, a section of Zhejiang Province, stretching from Hangzhou City to Changxing County, bordering Jiangsu Province. Due to the incomplete construction of the Jiangsu section, it cannot directly reach the capital. Business has not fully developed, and because it has not been open for long, the public is not yet accustomed to taking steamships and automobiles. Furthermore, a section is exclusively franchised by a commercial company, affecting business. Currently, the average daily income is approximately 600 yuan. Furthermore, the Hangmo section directly reaches Mogan Mountain, specifically for Chinese and foreign visitors in the summer. To facilitate travelers, joint transportation arrangements have been made with the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, which has been effective. In short, if the Beijing-Hangzhou road can be completed soon, business development is unlimited.

Yinfeng Section Yinfeng Section starts from Ningbo City and ends at Fenghua, an important route for eastern Zhejiang traffic. The section passes through areas rich in production, also handling freight transportation in addition to passengers, to aid in industrial and commercial development. Since its opening in May of the 18th year, it has gradually developed. The average daily income is now approximately 500 yuan. There are several branch lines on the entire line that have not yet been built. If they can all be completed, traffic will be more convenient, and business will naturally flourish even more.

Hangping Road Hangping Road opened to traffic in April of the 19th year. It now reaches Zhapu directly. The Zhapu-Pinghu section is still under construction and will soon be open to traffic. The road mostly follows the sea dike and is an earthen road. It must stop operating when it rains, making it difficult to develop business. The average daily income is only about 200 yuan. Efforts are currently being made to improve the road. If the entire road surface can be completed soon, it will not be difficult to develop business.

Hangchang Road Hangchang Road is a key route between Zhejiang and Anhui, with extremely important traffic. However, the Hangzhou-Yuhang and Yuhang-Lin'an sections have been contracted to the commercial Hangzhou-Yuhang and Yuhang-Lin'an companies. The Highway Bureau's construction only extends from Hualong to Changhua. To facilitate travel, it first opened the section from Hualong to Zaoxi in September of the 19th year and then continued the line from Zaoxi to Qianshan on October 1st. The Changhua section is expected to open to traffic within a month. Currently, the routes mostly pass through remote towns with few travelers. The average daily income is only about 50 yuan. In the future, once the entire Zhejiang-Anhui line is open to traffic, travelers between the two provinces will not have to detour, and the business prospects will naturally improve steadily.

Social News

The Most Ancient Newspaper 293

— Xian Liang

— London Newspaper Exhibition

On May 14th, the newspaper exhibition organized by Leder opened at the headquarters of the Institute of Journalism in London.

The exhibits include various British newspapers from the 17th, 18th, and 19th centuries. These newspapers from the past three centuries were collected by Mr. Andrews, the honorary curator of the London Institute of Journalism library. His collection this time is extremely rich, and the British public has indeed helped him a great deal. They generously participated in the exhibition with those very old newspapers and historically important records. Among them, the records of the trial and execution of Charles I are particularly valuable.

Many valuable ancient newspapers from Henry Hill are also very important exhibits in the exhibition. Henry Hill is the general manager of the British Hill Company. However, his valuable exhibits arrived late for the exhibition, and most of the visitors did not have the opportunity to appreciate them.

From those exhibits, many important records of newspapers can be found—

In 1588, the Spanish Armada's invasion of England was indeed the impetus for the emergence of newspapers. The appearance of the Armada itself was communicated throughout the country by beacon fires. At the same time, some writers reported news of the war through correspondence. Anyone who paid these writers could receive their correspondence.

Printed newspapers only officially became a tool for disseminating news when the "Thirty Years' War" broke out, but there was no fixed publication schedule.

On August 2, 1622, Nathaniel Butter published "Weekly News," which was the initial creation of a regular newspaper. "Weekly News" is still published today, but it has been changed to the words "God's Help."

On December 20, 1636, a woodcut picture called "The Strange Out-pouring of Fire" was published. This was the beginning of newspapers with pictures.

On March 11, 1705, The Daily Courant was published, which was the pioneer of daily newspapers.

In 1721, the first evening newspaper, The Evening Post, appeared.

In 1722, the oldest morning newspaper, The Morning Post, was published. Three copies of it are on display in the exhibition, and it is still being published in England today.

Economic Recovery Movement in the United States 294

A Twenty-Member Committee to Investigate and Research

New York News: The American Chamber of Commerce has now notified various local chambers of commerce to each recommend around fifteen experts to form committees, separately establishing departments for commerce, agriculture, and finance, etc., to thoroughly research methods for economic recovery. So far, committees have been organized for agriculture, urban development, domestic distribution, as well as nine departments such as finance, foreign trade, insurance, manufacturing industry, natural resources, production, and commercial associations. A total of twenty committees will be formed before the Chamber of Commerce's annual meeting in New York on June 26th and 27th. The International Chamber of Commerce also strongly supports this movement and is working together to promote it. Such a large-scale investigation into economic conditions and research into methods for economic recovery is a pioneering endeavor, and the initiators have high hopes for achieving results, it is said.

Exhibition of Works by Students Studying in Japan 295

Scheduled to Begin on the 24th

Tokyo News: An exhibition of works initiated by Chinese students studying in Japan, sponsored by the Japanese bookstore Tokyo-do, is scheduled to be held in the bookstore's upstairs space for one week starting on the 24th. The works are divided into categories of calligraphy, painting, sculpture, and seal carving, and are scheduled to be moved in before the 20th, it is said.

Ford Car Imports Increase by 30% 296

More Than 300 Vehicles Arrived Recently

This year, Ford's car imports to China from the United States have increased by approximately 30% compared to last year. Recently, the Liaoyang Maru of the Japanese international shipping company also brought 313 Ford passenger and cargo vehicles from the Ford factory in Yokohama to Shanghai.

League of Nations to Convene Colonial Conference 297

Restricting the Military Force of Colonial Police

Geneva News: The Council of the League of Nations plans to convene a conference on colonial issues in February of next year. The purpose is to find ways to restrict the use of all military weapons by police officers in various colonies. In recent years, the national liberation movements in colonies around the world have become increasingly fierce, and many are collaborating with the Third International. The Third International is using colonial national liberation movements to promote communism. The increase in colonial communism is due to the excessive oppression by the ruling countries. In view of this, the League of Nations plans to convene a conference to restrict the military weapons used by colonial police and to require each member state to report on the status of its colonies annually, it is said.

Eurasian Railway Fare Increased by 25% 298

Effective from the 15th of This Month

Tokyo News: Passenger tickets and small parcel freight rates for the Eurasian Railway through the Siberian Railway will be increased by 25% by the transportation authorities of all member countries, effective from the 15th of this month. In Japan, the transportation will be handled by ten stations: Tokyo, Yokohama, Nagoya, Kyoto, Osaka, Sannomiya, Kobe, Shimonoseki, Moji, and Nagasaki.
